Dissemination & Exploitation Accelerator: Solar Energy Helix 
The Solar Energy Helix will be created by P9 Crowdhelix (CHX) who will bring together a community of 150+ cross-
disciplinary and cross-sector stakeholders/actors across Europe and internationally, with attention to the Mediterranean 
and MPC countries. The focus will be on bringi ng together stakeholders from solar thermal energy and clean energy 
SMEs/industry organisations, and industry organisation with processes that require high reliability and high quality 
heat and cooling and continues operations, as well research organisations/researchers, associations and networks in 
solar thermal energy, that are interested in and are developing solar and thermal energy technologies, decarbonising 
the industrial sector, reducing dependency on fossil fuels and reducing emission of air pollutants.   
CHX is pan-European and International Open Innovation Network that connects and enables research organisations, 
SMEs and industry to collaborate, innovate and grow, and has a particular focus on developing collaborations and 
clusters around Horizon  2020 funding opportunities and accelerating the economic, environment and social impact 
from these collaborations. The network has more than 400+ member organisations from 42 countries, including all EU 
Member State countries, who have collectively won an  estimated + 4 billion in funding from Horizon 2020. The 
network is set-up around thematic areas/clusters (called “Helixes”), e.g. Energy Helix, Climate Helix, Manufacturing 
Helix,  Materials Helix and Digital Helix etc., and is supported by a technology p latform 
(https://www.crowdhelix.com/) where these virtual communities are hosted; please see the Helixes in Fig. 2.2 below.  
 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 29 
 
Figure 2.2 CHX Helixes (virtual communities) 
For the ASTEP project, CHX will establish the Solar Energy Helix, and link it with the existing Energy Helix, Climate 
Helix, Manufacturing Helix, Materials Helix and the Digital Helix. The Solar Energy Helix will be set-up and delivered 
in close collaboration with P2 ADSC (Coordinator), P5 DRA P7 EBOS, P8 EXERGY, P12 AMTP and 13 CRES, 
in order to support the consortium in accelerating and achieving its impact objectives, especially its exploitation 
strategy through engagement with industry end users, invest ors to ensure uptake of results following the end of the 
project, with focus on countries with limited or no application across the Mediterranean.  
The Helix will be centred on the ASTEP consortium and when it commences all  ASTEP partners will be given full 
access to the CHX network and platform free, for the duration of the project. Once the project has ended, everyone 
signed up will be able to retain their accounts for free (as external organisations), to ensure a self-sustaining community 
and continued collaboration among the partners, stakeholders and projects. It will then bring in interested organisations 
/ individuals from within its current membership base of 400+ organisations across 42 countries, first reaching out to 
members part of aligned Helixes (e.g. Energy Helix, Climate Helix, Manufacturing Helix, Materials and Digital Helix) 
ensuring engagement across the related Helixes, as well as across disciplines and sectors, including clean energy, 
renewable energy/solar thermal energy, and chemical engineering. It will reach out to stakeholders not yet members of 
the network to join the Helix (i.e. researcher organisations, industry/SMEs and associations, networks and clusters) 
across Europe and that are identified by the par tners through the stakeholder mapping activities. All external 
organisations and consortia that are invited or that contact ASTEP to join the Solar Energy Helix will be given 
immediate access to the Solar Energy Helix on the Crowdhelix platform and are not  required to become a full paying 
member of the CHX network. The Helix will also connect with other organisations and networks in the related fields 
across Europe (e.g. SPIRE cPPP, etc). It will link in/cluster with previously and other funded EU, as well other 
funded projects under this call, national and international projects in solar thermal energy , in particular for 
industrial processes, as well as decarbonisation of industry, reduced dependency on fossil fuels and reduced emission 
of air pollutants, to facilitate clustering of funded projects and maximize the EU investment driving the results to market 
uptake. To cluster with other funded projects, the Helix will first connect with the projects in which consortium 
members are leading/partnering. With  the Crowdhelix members having collectively won +4 billion of Horizon 2020 
funding, CHX will then reach out within the its network to connect other funded projects in the related areas that are 
lead and partnered by network members and connect them to the Solar Energy Helix , and in parallel connect with 
specific projects identified by the European Commission’s ASTEP Project Officer, including the other projects funded 
under this call. 
 
In practice, on the Crowdhelix Platform organisations and individuals cr eate profiles highlighting their expertise and 
knowledge, and post opportunities for collaboration. Please see Fig. 2.3 which is an example of a recent post and 
interaction from the Crowdhelix Platform. In the case of Helixes established around a Horizon 2020 projects, post will 
also disseminate project results and communicate upcoming project activities/events. On the adve nt of ever more 
powerful technologies in the area of machine learning, natural language processing, and artificial intelligence, an 
opportunity has arisen to augment the Crowdhelix Platform with a new software “recommender engine”. This system 
will dynamic ally suggest prospective collaborators for each opportunity posted, drawing its data from information 
provided by users of the platform, as well as information users have chosen to import from other relevant profiles. This 
system will also learn as it prog resses, to ensure that matches improve over time, all the while providing a direct 
incentive for Crowdhelix users to provide relevant and up-to-date information about their expertise and interests.  
 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 30 
      
Figure 2.3 Example of Academic and Industry Engagement on the Crowdhelix Platform 
 
The Solar Energy Helix and CHX’s “recommender engine” technology will not only facilitate faster dissemination of 
results to key stakeholders, but will also drive new forms of international, cross -disciplinary and cross -sectoral 
partnerships and open innovation activity in this area. The Helix will be set -up as a self-sustaining community hosted 
by CHX beyond the lifetime of the project, thereby promoting existing and creating new long-lasting impacts from the 
ASTEP project and supporting reach to the EU countries where such systems currently have very limited or no 
application according to SHIP. When the ASTEP project ends, the Solar Energy Helix will continue to be hosted on 
Crowdhelix’s platform, so that engagement continues (and grows) between all the stakeholders that have been brought 
into the network and this Helix, after the end of the project, and everyone signed during the project up will be able to 
retain their accounts for free (as external organisations), as well as have the option for their organisations to join as full 
members on the network.  The exiting helixes (20) are all strategically led by a  Research or Technology Organization 
member (RTO) of the network (e.g. Cardiff University leads the Energy Helix, University of Bergen leads the Climate 
Helix, Fraunhofer IWU leads the Manufacturing Helix, LEITAT Technology Centre leads the Materials Helix , and 
UCL leads the Digital Helix). As the strategy for the post project impact/exploitation is developed, the CHX Helix 
Manager will identify a RTO member, e.g. UPM, from the Helix that would be interested in strategically leading this 
Helix after the end of the project. This Helix and activities around this are support by the Crowdhelix team. 
 
In addition to the Crowdhelix Platform, CHX will organise 4 Helix Events, targeted to industry end-users and investors 
to connect and promote the outputs/results and uptake after the end of the project. The CHX Helix Manager will work 
support the Communication and Dissemination Activities so that CHX can plan how and what will be disseminated to 
the Solar Energy Helix Members through the Crowdhelix Platform, Events and CHX’s Newsletter, Twitter, LinkedIn, 
Facebook and Instagram accounts. 
 
Outline Business plan  
The commercialization of technologies developed during the ASTEP project will be executed through a detailed 
technology transfer and business plan carried out by the individual partners as well as joint undertakings and spin-offs 
in case of cross -cutting technologies. The project ensures the success of the European -based industry by creating a 
value chain and engaging with the potential stakeholders and eventual technology adopters. Greatcell Solar, as a 
consortium partner and end user, will conduct activities after the project towards final design and development of th e 
PSC pilot line, design verification, design validation and pilot line testing, whereas Flexbrick opens up the channels 
for engaging customers and creating sales leads for commercial sales at a later -stage. Below in Fig 2.4 is a business 
model canvas to highlight the approach to commercialization of ASTEP technology. 
 
The Business Plan will be a living document and will be updated and evolved throughout the project development. The 
business and exploitation plan will integrate several different commerciali sation phases including local, national, 
European and international level. Once the technology development phase is completed, the commercialisation will 
start at local level through interacting with local authorities and relevant department during the demonstration activities. 
Through the implementation of a well -developed dissemination and exploitation plan commercialisation period will 
continue at national, European and international levels. Partners such as UNED, UPM, VERT, DRA, ADSC, EXE will 
play a ke y role in developing international business relations with relevant parties and maximising the potential 
contribution of the solutions to the economic and technological growth. Briefly, in order to allow a smooth exploitation 
of

activities: 
• Business Models: Business plans will be based upon a succinct business model encapsulating for each key result 
taken forward; the value proposition, the configuration of the value creation, and the revenue model.

Market:

other industrial sectors.

The spin -off company will leverage the key importance of the consortium’s End -users to prove the 
technology to companies with similar needs. 
Financial Projection:  
We predict that further investment is needed to build a demo system (TRL7), which will suppose another 
3 years of developments. The spin-off company will search for additional financing not only from other 
European funded R&D programs such as ERANET, LIFE, RFCS, and H2020s but also from  national 
calls in the EU interested countries.   
Commercialisation Roadmap:  
The first step, once the project is finalised is to design and build a demo  to reach TRL 7 , which it is 
estimated that would last 2-3 additional years. After this period, a validation process is needed to obtain 
results for a year in order to obtain conclusions about the covered demand (KPI 5) and the estimated energy 
cost. To make the decision of a capital investment with regards to this new technology and without 
significant track records, a relevant economic advantage needs to be demonstrated. ASTEP will address 
this need demonstrating the innovative technologies under real industrial environments. A techno -
economic analysis for ASTEP demonstrators will be carried out with based on the est imated yearly 
thermal energy production [MWh]. An important reduction in cost is expected based in:

Every innovative project always has associated financial risk that the consortium plans to reduce through 
the research and development associated to the current proposal . The current proposal will  analyse 
potential commercial and production risks before going into the next step to commercialization including 
standardization analysis.

Strategy for management and protection of information/data and knowledge  
Management of Intellectual Property: 
Intellectual property (IP) generated within the project will be protected by patents, if appropriate, and its management 
will be regulated in compliance with the final consortium agreement and the intellectual property agreement among 
the partners. The consortium has identified three levels of Foreground (Results) IP which will be created in the course 
of the project: 
• Individual and joint IP, which belongs to individual partners or is jointly owned by partners working in a particular 
task and is restricted to those partners. 
• Generic IP, which can be used by all partners of the consortium. Some of the generic IP will be made more widely 
available to European academics, SME’s and other industrial organizations. 
• Publicly available IP which will be published at conferences, on the public web site and m ade available with no 
restrictions. 
 
The general principles for Intellectual Property Aspects set out by the EC for Horizon2020 projects will apply in 
ASTEP. Existing know how (background or pre -existing intellectual property) of a specific partner shall be made 
available on transfer conditions to the Partner(s) within the consortium. The use of such existing know -how is strictly 
limited for use to the achievement of the project goals and for the duration of the project. An overview of the existing 
know how will be included as an annex to the consortium agreement. Foreground shall be owned by the partner(s) who 
developed these results. Each partner is responsible for taking the appropriate steps for securing intellectual property 
of the knowledge or results created during the project. 
Results (resulting from the project): owned by one or more of the partners shall be licensed to other partners of the 
consortium on favourable conditions to the extent necessary to enable these partners to exploit their own results. 
Publication of results: The partners are entitled to publish the project results in the usual scientific form. However, all 
concept publications must be put on the website and submitted to all Partners together with a request for permission to 
publish. Requests for such permission to publish shall be responded to within one month of receipt thereof. An 
agreement is considered to have been granted if no objection is raised within a period of one month after submission 
of the manuscript to all par tners. One of the pages of ASTEP website will contain an overview and archive of all 
published information: scientific articles, publications, press releases, conference papers, etc. Publications will be 
submitted to reputable journals (using peer-review) that can provide “gold” open access (immediate open access mode) 
to reach the broadest possible audience for the results within a short space of time. More details on these issues will be 
described in the Consortium Agreement. 
 
Open access for scientific publishing:  
The Horizon 2020 main guidelines are directed to have research based on sustainable and inclusive economy with the 
important role of promoting knowledge and innovation in generating growth 12. Since the Project follows the H2020 
open access strategy for scientific publications, all the results that are publishable will follow an open-access model in 
order to optimize the impact of publicly funded scientific research, both at European level (FP7, Horizon 2020) and at 
Member State level. This way, E urope’s ability to enhance the economic performance of its companies and improve 
the capacity to compete through knowledge is improved.  
The results of the project can therefore be disseminated more broadly and faster, to the benefit of researchers, innovative 
industry and citizens. Even though it is believed that Open Access can also boost the visibility of European research, 
and in particular offer SMEs access to the latest research for utilisation, it has to be kept in mind that Open Access will 
not inte rfere with Consortium decisions to exploit project research outcomes commercially or by patent process. 
Therefore, the project will take into account the legitimate interests of the partners in terms of data protection and IPR 
issues relate to commercial impacts of project outcomes.   
ASTEP will develop and implement open access to the project research results according to the following main 
conditions: All peer reviewed research article will be deposited into on line repository, 2) To make the best effort to 
have open access to the articles with a delay (embargo) of 6 -12 months as maximum. ASTEP will encourage partners 
also at their Member State level to Open Access publishing and thus contribute to their coordination within the 
European Research Area. The consortium partners will follow the “gold” model, as they wish to maximise public and 
researcher access. Consequently, open access will be granted to all scientific publications resulting from the 
project.  
 
 
12 European commission. Horizon 2020 in a brief. ISBN: 978-92-79-33057-5 doi:10.2777/3719. Luxembourg.

Research Data Management: 
All partners will be responsible for publishing project results in local and international press (press releases or 
newsletters in magazines and newspapers, etc.) and in peer-reviewed scientific journals and conferences. As previously 
mentioned, RELA will maintain an overview of all published results and in cooperation with the Project Coordination, 
RELA will intervene in case of results that have been classified as publishable do not receive the necessary 
dissemination. In addition, the Consortium  will ens ure that all project related publications can be read online, 
downloaded and printed. However, as any additional rights such as the right to copy, distribute, search, link, crawl, and 
mine increase the utility of the accessible publication, efforts will be made to provide for as many of them as possible. 
Several open access schemes will be proposed for use to all consortium members. Depending on the nature, the 
importance, the cost and the available budget, a decision will be taken by the coordinator in coo peration with the 
Dissemination Manager  and the proposing partner as to the best open access scheme which is to be followed. A 
dedicated budget for open access scientific publications has been reserved, which will be used for “green” or “gold” 
publications in reputable journals. Alternative repositories such as the Open Access Infrastructure for Research in 
Europe (OpenAIRE), the Registry of Open Access Repositories (ROAR) and the Directory of Open Access 
Repositories (OpenDOAR) etc will be also exploited, as there are supported by the EC and there is no cost related to 
using these repositories. In all cases, as soon as possible and at the latest within six months after the publication is 
performed, RELA will be responsible to collect a machine-readable electronic copy of the published manuscript version 
in order to be deposited in the project website either as a reproduction, if permitted by the publisher, or as a direct link 
to the publication. In addition, the research data and bibliographic metadata needed to validate the results presented in 
the deposited scientific publications will be stored in the respective area of the repository. Finally, REL A will contact 
and exploit EC portals and tools (OpenAIRE, Horizon the EU Research and Innovation Magazine, research*eu results 
magazine, research*eu focus, etc.) in order to make the ASTEP generated knowledge publically available. Since the 
aforementioned tools provide free of charge, online access to the respective publications for any user, they will ensure 
open access of these publications. 
ASTEP participates in the Pilot Action on Open Access to Research Data which is part of the Horizon 2020 program. 
The goal is to provide, where possible, accurate and high -quality data to the research community so that the p roject 
will contribute to future advancements in the field of  thermal solar energy in industrial sites. A table summarizing the 
generated data, how it will be accessible (if possible) and how it will be preserved  will be released within DMP . 
Commercially sensitive data are declared confidential and described in the exploitation plan and Intellectual Property 
Rights (IPR) section. 
 
Data Management Plan (DMP): 
Over the projects’ life significant amounts of data will be produced as a result of ASTEP joint R&D activities. A data 
management plan is developed to set standards for protecting and managing the generated data and to maintain its 
integrity such that it is available during and after the project to its owners, stakeholders and/or the public depending on 
the level of confidentiality. Furthermore, a well-structured data plan minimizes the risk of loss of valuable data which 
would negatively impact future projects building on the results of the ASTEP project.  
Therefore, a DMP template will be developed using guidance provided by the EU and the Digital Curation Centre. The 
corresponding deliverable will be issued by M6.and will be updated as new data sets are produced during the project 
life. The purpose of the DMP is to provide an analysis of the main elements of the data management policy that will 
be used by the applicants regarding all the datasets that will be generated by the project. The DMP is not a fixed 
document but evolves during the lifespan of the project. The DMP should address the poi nts below on a dataset by 
dataset basis and should reflect the current status of reflection within the consortium about the data that will be 
produced.  
• Data set reference and name  
Qualification database of the materials/coatings produced with actual st andards and new protocols for PSC 
developments and testing. In addition, a separate dynamic data base will be created for storing modeling designs and 
data. Each individual partner has the choice to adapt their own code structuring for tracking development s such that it 
matches with their internal procedures. However, some guidelines will be developed to simplify identification of data 
for multi-partner use.  
• Data set description  
WP leaders are responsible for generating and/or collecting data within the ir WPs (i.e. BUL in WP2, UNED in WP3, 
UPCT in WP4, EXE in WP5, UPM in WP6, UPM in WP7, and VERT in WP8), sharing of data through the appropriate 
channels and delivery of the data set description. A private section within the ASTEP website will be dedicated  for 
storing and access to these data bases. The dataset description will clearly define the nature of the data (generated or 
collected), type of data (testing, modeling, literature/market research), potential use of the data/results (internal, 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 35 
benchmark, publication, etc.) and the to whom the data could be of value. Furthermore, links to other relevant data 
sources will be included such that exploitation of the final results will be easy. 
• Data sharing  
During the life of the project, data will be shared between the partners and the European Commission. After the end of 
the project, it will be discussed if and how the data or part of the data can be made available to external parties, by 
providing open access.  
• Archiving and preservation (including storage and backup)  
Through the website of the project, the data base will be shared with the partners and EU Commission, and if proceed 
to the external parties, with a lifetime of 5 years after the end of th e project. A fee will be foreseen in case the data is 
open to external parties in order to afford data base update and management. 
 
Communication activities13,14 
ASTEP is aligned with the Rome Declaration on Responsible Research and Innovation in Europe and is fully 
committed with the EC DG Research and Innovation’s main objective of fostering public engagement and sustained 
two-way dialogue between science and civil society. Moreover, general public awareness and acceptance of their active 
role in the renewable energy markets is crucial for the success of the energy transition. 
Therefore, an intensive Communication Plan will be implemented within ASTEP with the aim of e ngaging all the 
societal actors via inclusive participatory approaches. Communication plan will be consistently implemented 
throughout the whole lifetime of the project and will focus on two main areas and objectives: 
Internal communication management: The main objective is to keep a fluid interaction between project partners and 
to establish a transparent and accessible information sharing mechanisms. Communication between different partner 
subgroups to work on common goals or tasks will be always performed in an orderly and detailed way, making use of 
some of the many technological tools for teleworking, and following a clear methodology to establish at all times how 
work must be done together. Communication between partners will be supported mainly by tel ephone and 
videoconferences, email and face-to-face meetings. Besides, a restricted access area of the project’s website will allow 
project documents sharing and monitoring of the progress status of the project. The project coordinator will be 
responsible for launching and keeping updated this private area. 
External communication activities:  Communicating relevant knowledge about the project’s latest activities and 
achievements to the relevant identified ASTEP target audiences is certainly a way to keep all partners actively involved 
in the project and the ASTEP consortium accordingly realizes that communication is not something that should be dealt 
as a side task; on the contrary, it is one of the topmost aspects, priorities and prerequisites of running a s uccessful 
research project. In this context, the draft communication plan for promoting this project and its results, include an 
efficient and effective mix of both interpersonal and mass communication tools. Moreover, it shall be strongly 
emphasized, that for each targeted audience, a distinct strategy using targeted messages, means and language has been 
planned. Namely, specific audiences and communication methods have been defined for promoting ASTEP and its 
main results: 
• Direct proactive communications and physical demonstration: Attendance in seminars and conferences, one -
to-one communication, e-mailing stakeholders, periodic newsletters, etc.; 
• Clustering activities: Contacting parallel related projects, cross-field events; 
• Mass and general communication: Project website, press releases, posters and leaflets; 
• Scientific excellence: Publications in highly-ranked journals, presentations in conferences; 
• Academic: Conveyance of the new knowledge into University curricula, publications of MSc and PhD theses. 
Target Groups/End users: As already stressed above, an extremely imperative precondition so as to ensure augmented 
exploitation, high impact and increased likelihood of uptake of the project’s results, is to prudently and effectually 
disseminate and communicate the appropriate information to the relevant and interested audience; in a concise, well -
articulated, understandable and attractively packaged manner. Hence communicating the right information and 
messages to the right people, using the right language  and suitable means is the key to a successful dissemination 
strategy. In this context, by clearly identifying and classifying the different ASTEP target groups, the messages and 
information to be consigned to each of them as well as the communication language, measures and channels with which 
they shall be sent to each tier of audience, the likelihood of uptake of the project’s findings is exceedingly increased. 
In this regard, the following Table 2.8 presents the main communication measures to be used for effectively diffusing 
project related knowledge and information to each ASTEP target audience/end user as below. The aim of the 
communication activities within the project is to inform as many people as possible about the existence, the activities

Strategies for effective communication: As far as possible when communicating about ASTEP, the consortium will 
communicate impact (change) of the action instead of communicating on administrative or procedural milestones. The 
consortium will make a concerted effort to find more effective ways to communicate impact, through storytelling as

regionally, nationally and globally and thus, create wider engagement. 
 
3 IMPLEMENTATION
3.1 Work plan — Work packages, deliverables  
Overall description /graphical description 
The project is divided into 9 work-packages (WP), each with its own tasks, deliverables and associated milestones 
in order to facilitate implementation and monitoring of progress. First, the project management activities are centered 
in WP1. The End-user requirements for the prototypes Testing at the Industrial Sites are centered in WP2. The different 
technologies that will be developed in the proposal are: Application of SunDial Technology to the Solar Concept 
(WP3), Application of Energy Storage to the So lar Concept (WP4), Combined ASTEP Specification Design 
(WP5). The state of the art of the partners’ knowledge implemented in WP3-WP5 begins the actual proposal at TRL3. 
The different technologies are implemented and tested in the different partner’s laboratory in Construction, Testing 
and Validation of ASTEP (WP6) to lead the proposal to  TRL4. Finally, the complete concept proposal is tested in  
ASTEP Concept at Industrial Sites (WP7) at 2 End-Users (Arcelor Mittal Tubular Products Iasi (AMTP), and 
Mandrekas (MAND), using the ASTEP Concepts to test them at their Industrial Sites under Operational conditions 
to lead the project to the objective  TRL 5. A very important featur e of the current proposal is to assess the 
Sustainability Assessment of the Concept proposal  (WP8) not only in  a favorable geographical location, (lower 
than 40ºN Latitude for MAND acting as End-user), but also in a more unfavorable location (such as AMTP acting as 
End-User located in Iasi (Romania) at 46.7ºN). Finally, a key activity of the project is the definition of how the project 
developments are exploited, disseminated and communicated to the different stakeholders at Communication, 
Dissemination and Exploitation (WP9). 
 
WPs are described in Table 3.1a, the combined work effort of the project is summarized in Table 3.1b. The respective 
deliverables for each Work Package are listed in Table 3.1c. Each WP is led by a project partner experienced in the 
corresponding area, to ensure the best practice and work efficiency. The approach described in section 1.3 will ensure 
the correct testing of the technologies at the two (2) end-user’s facilities. 
The Program Evaluation Review Technique (PERT) chart showing the WP interdependencies among the different WPs 
and tasks is shown in Figure 3.1 while the Gantt Chart showing the timing of the Work Packages is shown in Figure 
3.2. The potential risks have been identified and contingency plans proposed (discussed in Section 3.2 under “ Critical 
risks and mitigation measures”).

Objectives: 
The main objectives of this Work Package are: 
• To establish efficient operation of all project bodies, including proper decision making and conflict 
resolution at all levels. 
• To ensure required quality of project work and its results as well as to perform self -assessment and 
corresponding project monitoring, including risk management. 
• To organise overall project administration and supervision of financial flows as well as communication 
with EC and project reporting. 
• To provide necessary environment for collaboration within the consortium. 
• To lay down a set of tools and procedures in order to keep the documentation up -to-date, consistent and 
available for all the consortium members. 
Description of work  
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 41 
Task 1.1 – Work plan, Coordination and Document Management (M1 – M48) Leader: UNED, Participant: 
ADSC. This task involves overall project planning, coordination (including internal project meetings, 
communication strategy and working environment) and management of the documentation that must be generated. 
This documentation will be used during the project  according to the management principles and structures laid 
down in Section 3.2 . Additionally, this documentation will set up the necessary internal p roject meetings, 
communication strategy and working environment to enable the objectives of the project to be completed.  
Considering self -assessment activities, quality assurance and management of risks, external project relevant 
factors, decision making  process and conflict management. The coordinator in this respect is responsible for 
supporting effective working, verifying that the technical information and action tasks are described in Table 3.1. 
Finally, the coordinator will c ontrol that deadlines  are met, quality control, communication organization and 
meeting among consortium partners, ensuring high-level project representation. 
Task 1.2 - Administrative and Financial Management (M1 – M48) Leader: UNED. This task covers the 
operation and maintenance of the project administrative and management infrastructure. It also includes the 
financial control and management of resources and the coordination of internal affairs as well as maintaining the 
EC’s relationship with the project. Through esta blishment of the Project Secretariat, this task will assure overall 
project administration and communication, project reporting, preparation of management reports and internal 
project reviews, administration of project meetings at all levels, keeping project accounts, etc. 
Task 1.3 -Advisory Board Management  (M1 – M48) Leader: UNED, Participant: External Advisory 
Members. The Advisory Board will be formed by external experts that will advise strategically the consortium. 
The composition of the Advisory Boar d will be heterogeneous, including expertise from different sectors, not 
specifically related to technological research objectives. Currently the External Advisory members as their support 
Letters are incorporated in the Section 4 of the current proposal are: 
• Joao Paulo Oliveira acting as Executive Administrator from “ The Navigator Company ”, leading pulp 
and paper company in Portugal 
• Cristina Cristalli acting as Research and Innovation Director from “ Loccioni”, leading Italian service 
provider in energy and manufacturing.  
• David Gallego Martínez acting as Manager from “Regenera Levante”, leading Spanish service provider 
in thermal energy. 
In this task all the aspects related to the management of the Advisory Board will be handled, that is: coordination; 
meeting organization; distribution of documents and exchange of information. The task is aiming to gather relevant 
knowledge to implement the technological improvement of ASTEP prototypes and to generate key ideas for future 
exploitation and development of business plans. Each Advisory Board meeting will generate minutes and a set of 
recommendations. 
Task 1.4 -Overall Quality and Risk Control (M1 – M48), Leader: UNED, Participant: ADSC. This task is 
completely devoted to the continuously monitoring and management of possible risks that may arise during the 
implementation of the project. As described in Section 3.2, several risks may occur, and proper solutions need 
to be taken in order to treat th em without affecting the expected outcomes of the project. For this reason, the 
coordinator along with the Project Management Committee support will continuous ly monitor the proceeding of 
the project and participation of the project beneficiaries to the wo rk carried out within the project. So, to easily 
identify possible risks and be able to take fast contingency actions and decisions about them. Additionally, to 
control and mitigate any risk, the task will be devoted to guarantee quality of the different activities and outcomes 
from the project. 
Task 1.5 – Data and Ethical Management, Planning and Assessment (M 1-M48), Leader: UNED, 
Participant: ADSC. Through this task, data materializing during the project will be analysed, and a Data and 
Ethical Management document will be delivered, identifying best practices and specific standards. It will take into 
account ethical and Intellectual Property (IPR) related constraints, for access, storage and curation of data collected 
during project’s activities (WP2-WP8). For this reason, guiding principles and procedures regarding privacy, data 
protection, legal issues and ethical challenges will be considered. Data suitability for sharing and reuse, in 
accordance with existing legislation framework and ethical requirements is guaranteed while satisfying the need 
of open access and open data guidelines of the EC will be assured. This document will be maintained and updated 
during the project, fully addressing the lifecycle of data generated at various phases of ASTEP. The Consortium 
Agreement will establish detailed processes for IPR management ASTEP Project Legal and Ethics Committee will 
incorporate European and national ethical and legal requirements. 
Role of Main Partners:  UNED will coordinate the WP and the p roposal assisted by the partners ADSC and 
EBOS.

Objectives. 
The main objectives of this Work Package are: 
• To obtain thermal demand profiles of the SPIRE and other industrial sectors (Level 1) and identify the key 
performance indicators of the System 
• To obtain the thermal demand profiles developed for End-users. 
• To investigate integration strategies and design a demonstration rig capable of meeting the demonstration 
objectives keeping in mind the economic & commercial objectives. 
Description of work 
T2.1 Level 1 Thermal demand profile and definition of KPIs for ASTEP system (M1 -M5) Leader: BUL, 
Participant: All This task will review and identify the thermal demand profiles of several diverse industry sectors 
(including SPIRE, food processing, agricultural) and list the typical heating and cooling requirements and 
individual key performance indicators, design req uirements and operational limits (hours of operation, min/max 
temp) taking into account location and climate data and will be included as part of D2.1 report. The findings will 
be used to develop different industry application scenarios for the ASTEP modul ar system and be compared in 
WP5. 
T2.2 Level 2 End-users scenario Analysis and Development (M5-M9) Leader: SUN Participant: All 
This task examines potential end-user variations for the full-scale ASTEP modular system: 
• End-user Context 1 and 2 – Heat demand bias (temperature levels and heating hours) for AMTP and MAND 
• End-user Context 2 – Cooling demand bias (temperature levels and cooling hours) for MAND. 
• End-user Context 1 and 2 – Increasing energy storage infrastructure (demand response balancing) for AMTP 
and MAND. 
It will investigate and develop each scenario and produce schematics which go beyond the basic demonstration rig 
setup. This will involve, for example, designing compatible intelligent heating networks for each of the two sites 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 43 
(and cooling for the MAND site) and, analysing thermal storage integration. It will report on heat demand profiles, 
heat supply performance, demand response and commercial aspects relevant to industrial partners (e.g. 
summarising relevant financial incentives). The report will also provide data which will be used for the blockchain 
interactive and smart digital platform. The findings generated in this task will feed in to the tailored ASTEP design 
for the 2 End-users.  
T2.3 Concept Design Development (M1-M9) Leader: BUL, EXE Participant: All 
This task will outline the whole system in order to provide a preliminary concept design, searching for compatible 
and high efficiency SFR-heat pump/energy storage systems and integration strategies.  
 The report will also confirm key research schedules necessary in subsequent WPs which will be carried out to 
develop the state -of-the-art and to finalise equipment and system specifications. An initial concept report that 
provides a starting point for mod elling and research/engineering of the individual components in WP3 -5 will be 
developed and reviewed in a consortium meeting. 
Role of Main partners: BUL will coordinate the WP with information provided by AMTP and MAND and shared 
tasks with SUN and EXE to obtain the thermal demands from End-users.

Objectives.  
The main objectives of this Work Package are:  
• Optical design and optimisation of the SunDial Fresnel collectors for each application and latitude. 
• Thermal-hydraulic design and optimisation of the receivers to accomplish the thermal requirements of 
the industry processes. 
• Analysis of the daily and yearly operation of the two end-user’s systems. 
• Thermo-mechanical analysis of the receiver and heat exchangers and link to the thermal stores. 
• Design of the control strategies and selection of the sensors and actuators. 
• Detailed design of the SunDial Fresnel collectors. 
Description of work 
T3.1 Basic design of Sundial for AMTP (M3-M18). Leader: UNED, Participants: AMTP, UPM, EXE, 
ADSC, DRA 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 44 
The preliminary design of the rotary Fresnel system for the application of AMTP will be addressed. In this case, 
the Sundial design will consist on a rotary platform containing several rows of rotating mirrors concentrating the 
irradiation to the linear receiver. Mirrors and receiver, which are parallel to each other, are installed onto a rotating 
structure. This platform will turn around a vertical axis so that the sun is always within the collector transversal 
plane. At the same time, mirrors will rotate around their longitudinal axis in order to reflect onto the receiver as 
the sun altitude varies. Thus, the system follows the Sun using a two-axis tracking system, i.e. the platform rotates 
with the sun’s azimuthal angle and the tilting angle of the mirrors change following the solar altitude. UNED leads 
the task and is responsible for the receiver design, aide d by UPM and ADSC. The kind of tube will be selected 
(evacuated or not evacuated, diameter, module length, etc.) as well as the selective coating and the secondary 
reflector characteristics. UPM is responsible for the solar field optimisation, aided by UNE D, including the 
geometric design of the mirrors, number of rows, width, optical properties, diameter and tilt of the platform, etc. 
The design will be addressed from  theoretical calculations and simulation tools. All the mathematical and 
numerical models will be developed ad -hoc for the project. They will be implemented in Matlab (or any similar 
tool). EXE, BUL and DRA will provide the information regarding the thermal requirement from the industrial 
processes.  
T3.2 Basic design of Sundial for MAND. (M3-M21). Leader: UNED, Participants: UPM, E XE, ADSC, 
DRA, MAND 
The preliminary design of the rotary Fresnel system for the application of MAND will be addressed. In this case, 
the Sundial design will consist of a rotary platform containing several rows of fix ed mirrors concentrating the 
irradiation on the linear receiver.  Mirrors and receiver, which are parallel to each other, are installed onto a rotating 
structure. This platform will turn around a vertical axis so that the sun is within the collector symmetry plane at all 
times (Fig. 2). Thus, the system follows the Sun using a one-axis tracking system, i.e. the platform rotates with the 
Sun’s azimuthal angle. UNED leads the task and is responsible for the receiver design, aided by UPM and ADSC. 
The kind of tube will be selected (evacuated or not evacuated, diameter, module length, etc.) as well as the selective 
coating and the secondary reflector characteristics. UPM is responsible for the solar field optimisation, aided by 
UNED, including the geometric design of the mirrors, number of rows, width, optical properties, diameter and tilt 
of the platform, etc. 
The design will be addressed form theoretical calculations and simulation tools. All the mathematical and 
numerical models will be developed ad -hoc for the project. They will be implemented in Matlab (or any similar 
tool). EXE and BUL will provide the information regarding the thermal requirement from the industrial process. 
T3.3 Optimisation of Daily and Yearly Operation of Sundial. (M6-M21). Leader DRA, Participants: 
UNED, UPM, DRA, AMTP, MAND, EXE 
Once the devices are outlined, in this task their performance will be evaluated and optimised. For that, the 
simulation at design condition and at part load operation of the Sundial is required. Th is simulation will be done 
using ad -hoc codes developed by UNED and UPM for this purpose. Also, the characterisation of the typical 
working day and meteorological year for the site of each End-User is needed. 
In a second step, the systems will be optimised to maximize the production, according to the requirements provided 
in WP2. Finally, the dynamics of the systems will be assessed. The evaluation will be carried out again using 
simulation codes developed ad-hoc. In this case, TRNSYS and/or Open Modellica will be used as simulation tools. 
UNED leads the task and is responsible for the steady state and transient simulations. UPM aids in the optimization 
process. DRA will assist with matching of the system operation with the thermal storage units. 
T3.4 Preliminary Thermo-Mechanical Analysis. (M6-M21), Leader ADSC, Participants: UNED, DRA 
This task aims to the thermal -hydraulic validation and thermo -mechanical analysis of the receiver and heat 
exchangers. This analysis will include environmental load factors in fluence on optical and thermal conversion. 
The analysis will be done using CFD simulation codes, particularly Ansys-CFX. ADSC will lead the task and will 
be responsible for the CFD simulations. UNED aids ADSC in the thermal -mechanical analysis of the syste ms, 
including the thermal -mechanical stress analyses, fatigue calculation and life prediction in order to estimate 
whether the initial design should be considered as valid or, on the contrary, some modifications are required. 
T3.5 Development of Control Strategies and Identification of Suitable Electronics/Sensors (M6-M21). 
Leader: IRIS, Participants: UPM, UNED, ADSC 
Once the basic designs for the two end users are defined, IRIS will establish the most adequate control strategy by 
integrating proper commercial sensors for monitoring the SunDial Technology (sun irradiance, temperatures, heat 
transfer fluid flow, etc.), designing the required electronic systems for signal conditioning and telecommunications, 
as well as defining robust and real-time control strategies for guaranteeing proper behaviour of the system. Further 
integration for the whole ASTEP control system will be performed in task 5.4 
T3.6 Detailed design of Sundial for AMTP and MAND (M12-M21) Leader: UPM Participants: UNED, 
DRA, ADSC, IRIS 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 45 
In this task, the final and detailed design s of the systems for both end-users and sites are defined. The definition 
includes the selection of materials, drawings and a cost evaluation. UPM leads th is task, aided by UNED and 
ADSC in the drawings and selection of materials. 
Role of Main Partners: UNED will coordinate this WP sharing tasks with ADSC, UPM to design two (2) SunDial 
rotary Fresnel collectors. 
Deliverables

Objectives.  
The main objectives of this Work Package are: 
• Design of the hybrid thermal energy storage system, considering three subsystems:  
o PCM selected for two end-user’s requirements;  
o Shell-side insert;  
o Active hydraulic circuit and regulation. 
• Selection of the optimal geometry  for the inserts and multi -tube system, by means of modelling and 
simulation of the unsteady heat transfer phenomena during charging and discharging of heat energy in the 
storage system. Selection of metal alloy -based materials for the  inserts and assess investment casting and 
assembly procedures. 
• Overall analysis of the storage systems and their integration with the solar collectors. 
Description of work 
T4.1 Basic Design (M3-M18). Leader UPCT Participants: UNED, UPM, DRA, PWR 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 46 
This task is devoted to the definition of the overall engineering aspects of the energy storage system. Integration 
with the overall solar system and with the end user application s (steel industry and food sector)  will be the first 
objective, aiming at defining: a) heat transfer flui d (HTF), accordingly with the SunDial Fresnel collector design 
and operational conditions; b) flow rate of HTF and expected range of inlet temperatures, following the wide 
irradiance conditions in the end users location; c) maximum energy storage capacity.  
Likewise, the concept design of the active hydraulic circuit will be accomplished in this task. The engineering 
strategy for controlling the velocity for energy charging and discharging will be defined, based on a variable 
hydraulic resistance of the heat transfer fluid path through the energy storage system. 
T4.2 Modelling, CFD Simulation, and Optimization (M3-M21). Leader ADSC Participants: UPCT 
This task is aimed at selecting the thermal conductivity enhancement method  in the shell of the energy storage 
system. This will be followed by selecting the dimensions and distribution pattern of the selected method(s). It is 
possible that two methods will be selected, as heat storage media operating at two different temperatures are needed 
for the two prototypes.  Likewise, the modelling of the energy charging and discharging cycles under solar 
irradiance coupling conditions will be performed. 
Optimization routines will be considered for defining insert design that minimizes the metal weight yielding the 
best charging and discharging velocities. Some restrictions, like the shape of the inserts, the size and distribution 
of the heat transfer fluid conduits, and the mechanical strength of the overall system – based on the thermal cycle 
stresses – will be imposed. As a result of this task, a CAD model will be delivered to task T.4.3, for 3D printing of 
a polylactide polymer model. 
The understanding of the physical mechanisms that involve melting and solidification in the hybrid thermal energy 
storage system will be accomplished by means of numerical modelling and simulation. The coupling of the energy 
storage tank with the Fresnel collector, which works under continuously variable conditions, will be implemented 
in a CFD code for a proper modelling of the energy charging cycle. The discharging cycle will be described through 
a coupling of the  Thermal Energy Storage  (TES) with the end user application  (two being involved in this 
proposal). 
T4.3 Selection and Definition of Materials and Manufacturing  (M6-M21). Leader PWR. Participant: 
DRA 
This task will focus on the choice of PCM materials and manufacturing methods for PCM -based thermal energy 
storage units characterized by the high rate of charging and regulated rate of discharging and large storage capacity. 
At least two test units for composite PCMs storage systems shall be implemented and validated according to the 
criteria given by end-users. PCMs will be selected considering the appointed melting range (exceeding 175 °C or 
230 °C), possibly from multi -component mixtures of salts with high latent heat and low chemical affinity to 
aluminium inserts – a possible candidate for study will include sodium nitrate. Spatial metal inserts made of Al-Si 
alloys, characterized by a thermal conductivity of ≈164 W/m·K will be produced and applied in order to enhance 
the heat transfer within the energy storage units between outside source of heat and the PCM. The cho sen 
manufacturing technology of metal inserts (heat exchangers) consists of the following steps; FDM (Fused 
Deposition Modelling) realized by 3D printing from polymer, forming of the ceramic mould, removal of the 
polymer pattern by burning off and subsequent investment casting of the metal alloy in the mould cavity. Previous 
research confirmed the suitability of polylactide (PLA) polymer for 3D printing pattern which can be very quickly 
designed. Applied investment casting results in the manufacturing of exact copy of polymer pattern characterized 
by its complicated geometry. For complete filling of very intricate moulds the eutectic aluminium alloy AC 44200 
with good fluidity and thermo -physical properties can be used. Other Al-based alloys characterized by the k 
value of over 200 W/m K will be taken into consideration.  Modelled spatial designs of Al alloy-based inserts 
(heat exchangers) will be tested, but the particular emphasis will be placed on the honeycomb structures, because 
of their beneficial properties such as high stiffness and stress fatigue resistance. The design of the Al based inserts 
(heat exchangers) should ensure the mechanical resistance to stresses caused by the change of the coefficients of 
thermal expansion of the PCM during its phase transformation.   
The manufactured spatial elements with central pipe for the transportation of the heat transfer fluid will be joined  
by mechanical methods or by developed brazing method and by this way the large spatial element as the inside 
heat exchanger of the accumulator with the parallel and serial connections will be created.  
The two energy storage systems characterized by the above described design with the mixed insulation system 
(conventional and vacuum) will be built.  
T4.4 Overall Analysis of Storage System (M6-M21). Leader DRA Participants: UPCT 
The integration of the heat stores, the thermal fluid transfer mechanisms and the connection with the Fresnel solar 
collectors will be examined in detail to ensure that the thermal stores will meet the requirements of the two 
prototypes for the steel and f ood processing applications. This will be carried out in conjunction with Task 4.5 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 47 
below, as instrumentation and sensors to affect the control of the systems will, in many instances, need to be 
included within the stores and/or other components during the assembly process. Of particular importance will be 
the impact of changes in solar input during the times when solar energy is available, and the potential deterioration 
of storage potential in periods when the store is the only unit supplying the process heat (or, in the case of the food 
sector unit), cooling via the absorption chiller. 
T4.5 Development of Control Strategies and Identification of Suitable Electronics/Sensors (M6-M21). 
Leader: IRIS Participants: UPCT, DRA 
IRIS will design and implement the control strategy for the hybrid thermal energy storage system. Specific 
sensors for monitoring this technology will be selected (flow, temperature, pressure) and integrated. All the 
electronics systems will be taken into consideration and a reliable real-time control strategy will be put in place 
to assure proper performance of the system. Further integration for the whole ASTEP control system will be 
performed in task 5.4 
Role of Main partners: UPCT and PWR will share the development of the Thermal Energy Storage assisted by 
ADSC and DRA performing specific tasks. 
Deliverables  
Deliv. (No.) Deliverable name, Lead, Type, Diss. Level, Del. Time 
D4.1 Engineering configuration of the Thermal Energy Storage system, UPCT, PU, R, M18 
The thermal-hydraulic design of the TES system is reported including number of tubes, shell-
side inserts, heat transfer fluid and mass flow rates. 
D4.2 Modelling and simulation of the charging and discharging cycles of the TES. ADSC, 
PU, R, M21 
Analysis of the TES performance using CAE tools such as CFD 
D4.3 Selection and Definition of Materials and Manufacturing, PWR/UPCT/DRA, CO, R, 
M15/M18/M21 
• PCM selection and characterization. PWR, CO, R, M15 Phase change materials 
for each end user’s application will be selected and its thermal properties will be 
characterized. 
• Design of inserts for different end user’s applications, UPCT, CO, R, M18 The 
geometrical design of the shell-side inserts will be assessed for each application, 
using optimization routines 
• Assessment of the PCM insert manufacturing method and assembly.

Objectives.  
The main objectives of this Work Package are:  
• To define and numerically validate the individual components of the innovative ASTEP system and to 
develop an integrated model to facilitate system design with outputs from (WP3, WP4) 
• Study the critical design pathway with respect to the sizing and connectivity of the individual components 
and evaluate the design space against the conceptual demand profiles developed in WP2.  
• Produce designs for the integration of the ASTEP system to satisfy the thermal demands of the End -User 
Industrial sites highlighted in WP2 
• Validation and optimisation of the numerical model under simulation environment. 
• To integrate the overall control strategies of the units (WP3, WP4) for management of the integrated 
ASTEP system in real time. 
Description of work 
T5.1 Conceptual design of the ASTEP System (M3-M18). Leader: EXE, Participants: UNED, UPM, UPCT, 
DRA 
Component sub -models will be developed and integrated to form an overall dynamic system model under 
simulation environment. The component models will initially be validated using data from the literature and later 
using data obtained from tests of the deve loped components from WP 3 & 4. The overall system model will be 
developed to enable optimisation of design and control of the system and will have the capability to allow 
evaluation of the system performance with different component sizes and process conf igurations under different 
climate locations in order to satisfy thermal demand profiles with multiple heating and cooling requirements. 
T5.2 Simulation of the Thermodynamic Performance of the ASTEP system (M6 -M21). Leader: EXE 
Participants: UNED, UPM, UPCT, DRA 
This task will develop the specific design methodology for the ASTEP system using the model developed in task 
5.1. The design process will involve sizing, connectivity and scheduling for the components of the system: solar 
thermal, thermal storage, chiller (for one site, MAND), in order to meet the range of thermal demand profiles 
developed in WP2, leading to an assessment of the application of the ASTEP technology in a number of industrial 
scenarios. Design temperatures, working fluid(s), mass flow and other thermodynamic requirements will be 
determined in this task. The key performance indicators defined at WP2 will be analysed and included in the report. 
The design methodology will consider the stochastic nature of solar thermal generation and the design 
methodology will incorporate a target for the likelihood of the system to completely meet the thermal demand. 
This target, e.g., 95%, will be an important part of the design specification since it will capture the trade -off 
between system size (and therefore cost) and the fraction of the thermal demand met by solar energy. 
T5.3 Overall Integrated System Designs and Simulations of the ASTEP system for End-User cases (M6 -
M21). Leader: EXE Participants: UNED, UPM, UPCT, DRA 
Using the methodology develop ed in T5.2, two designs will be produced specifically tailored to the demands of 
the industrial partners, according to the requirements and geographical locations identified in WP2. The predicted 
performance of the designs will be assessed using the integr ated process model and component level design 
requirements will be provided to the partners such that the prototypes components fabricated in WP6 will meet the 
needs of the integrated systems. As a result of this task, a multi-parametric matrix which includes all the key design 
and operational parameters, will be produced. The results of these simulations will feed into the demonstration and 
validation activities. The results will be compared against the monitoring results during the last phase of the project. 
T5.4 Integration of Control Strategies and Optimization of ASTEP system performance (M6-M21). Leader: 
IRIS Participants: EXE, UNED, UPM, UPCT, DRA 
In this task different integrated plant wise control strategies will be designed and evaluated,  based on the unit 
control and instrumentation systems defined for both the Sun Dial technology (task 3.5) and the thermal energy 
storage system (task 4.5). Dynamic transient simulation using a virtual absorption machine will be performed by 
EXE, helped by  the outgoing experimental data. The available solar radiation determines the operating 
temperatures of the cycle, hence the importance of developing a control strategy that would maximize the available 
solar energy through the system operation under parti al load in an anticipated way. Managing a common heat 
generator to produce heating and cooling loads, requires regulation strategies that manage the optimal operating 
conditions and transients in each case. Therefore, this task will set up a framework for learning the energy needs, 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 49 
controlling, seeking to optimise the ASTEP system performance and meet  the end user requirements, for both 
heating and cooling requirements. 
Role of Main partners:  EXE will lead the integrated ASTEP system design assisted by IRIS  in the control 
strategies development. 
Deliverables

combined system.

Objectives. 
The main objectives of this Work Package are: 
• Construction and installation of ASTEP concepts of the three main sub -systems: solar field, storage and 
integrated control system. 
• Tests of the three sub-systems under constrains stated by AMTP for different solar inputs. 
• Tests of the three sub-systems under constrains stated by MAND for different solar inputs. 
• Integration of sub -systems results, including data from WP3, WP4, and WP5, in a global model for 
revaluation to advance from TRL3 to TRL 4. 
Description of work 
T6.1 SunDial ASTEP component procurement, construction, installation and tests. (M21-M27). Leader: 
UPM Participant: UNED, IRIS 
During this task two ASTEP concentrators will be built using the design resulting from WP3 for both AMTP and 
MAND and tested during several months. As a result of the task, a complete model of the system must be obtained, 
which includes steady state operation, start up and shut off. UPM will lead this task, which will include the 
following sub-tasks: 
T6.1.1 Construction of ASTEP concentrator. Leader: UPM. Participant: UNED, IRIS 
UPM will lead this sub-task. The two ASTEP concentrators will be built in Tecnogetafe, close to Madrid. 
UPM will lead the installation of the solar platform, including the structure, mirrors, receivers and rotating 
joint. UNED will carry out the installation of an external heat exchanger, where the atmosphere will be 
the system heat sink. It must be developed so that exhaust air temperature is safe at operating conditions. 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 50 
IRIS will implement the control system in order to  operate both prototypes: rotation of the platforms, 
rotations of mirrors for AMTP, pumping system operation and defocusing in case of critical temperatures. 
As a requirement for the ASTEP concentrators´ installation, common materials accessible in any loc al 
industry must be used in order to achieve a higher social impact.  
As a result of this sub-task, both ASTEP concentrators must be installed and fully operating for the tests.  
T6.1.2 Testing of AMTP ASTEP concentrator. Leader: UPM, Participant: UNED, IRIS 
UPM will lead this sub-task together with the collaboration of UNED, whereas IRIS will be in charge of 
the control system. First, a series of test for heating the system up and cooling down will be carried out. 
The objective of these tests will be to ac hieve temperature requirements given by AMTP while avoiding 
receiver damages due to thermal stresses. These tests will be developed first during the morning/afternoon, 
when the sun altitude is low and, thus, when the solar impin ging power is limited. Then,  tests will be 
carried out at midday, in order to simulate system heating for summer days. Then, continuous operation 
of the ASTEP concentrator will be tested for different days with important sun altitude variations 
(summer, spring and autumn). As a resul t of this sub-task, a relevant amount of data will be available in 
order to develop a model to integrate the AMTP solar field with the storage system and the ASTEP system.  
T6.1.3 Testing of MAND ASTEP concentrator. Leader: UPM Participant: UNED, IRIS 
UPM will lead this sub-task together with the collaboration of UNED, whereas IRIS will be in charge of 
the control system. First, a series of test for heating the system up and cooling down will be carried out. 
The objective of these tests will be to achie ve temperature requirements given by MAND while avoiding 
receiver damages due thermal stresses. These tests will be developed first during the morning/afternoon, 
when the sun altitude is low and, thus, when the solar imping power is limited. Then, tests wi ll be carried 
out at midday, in order to simulate system heating for summer days. Then, continuous operation of the 
ASTEP concentrator will be tested for different days with important sun altitude variations (summer, 
spring and autumn). As a result of this  sub-task, a relevant amount of data will be available in order to 
develop a model to integrate the MAND solar field with the storage system and the ASTEP system.  
T6.2 Storage system ASTEP storage system, procurement, construction,  installation and test. (M21-
M27). Leader: UPCT Participant: UPM, UNED, EXE, DRA, IRIS 
During this task a n ASTEP PCM storage system will be built and tested, employing the design resulting from 
WP4. UPCT will lead this task, which will include the following sub-tasks:  
T6.2.1 Construction of storage system. Leader: UPCT, IRIS, PWR 
As a result of this sub -task, two different ASTEP storage systems, working with different PCMs for the 
requirements of the test sites, will be installed for melting and solidification tests under realistic operating 
conditions. UPCT will lead this sub -task, PWR will assist with the integration of inserts  into the overall 
heat exchange equipment, and IRIS will implement the control system in order to operate  a controlled 
discharge process. The mechanical design will allow for a substitution of the phase change material, in 
order to test different PCMs. A cooling circuit will be employed to dissipate the stored energy in the TES, 
allowing for conducting discharging cycle tests.  
T6.2.2 Testing of storage system. Leader: UPCT. Participants: UPM, UNED, EXE, IRIS 
UPCT will lead this sub -task, where UPM and UNED  will collaborate in defining the charging 
requirements of the storage system whereas EXE and B UL will define the discharging requirements  and 
IRIS will be in charge of the control system . A  controlled electrical resistance, able to provide an 
irradiance-like variable heat source, will be employed for heating the heat transfer fluid during the charging 
cycle. First, tests will be carried out for steady state requirements under different thermal power exchange 
inputs. Then, a series of tests under transient power requirements will be carried out, including 
requirements given by AMTP and MAND solar fields.  A full characterization of the charging and 
discharging dynamics will be provided, as well as heat transfer coefficients during melting and 
solidification in the shell side of the TES. 
T6.3 Absorption heat pump and heat exchanger , procurement and interface system development.  (M21-
M27) Leader: EXE Participant: BUL, IRIS, DRA 
In order to ensure that the enhanced solar concentrator designs, it will be necessary to consider various 
commercially available small-scale absorption chillers and associated components e.g. heat exchangers. Based on 
activities and component selection in WP5, suitable absorption chiller devices, and other components will be 
purchased, and a design will be developed for an interface system that will couple the collector output to a low -
cost absorption chiller for MAND requirements. Once refined, a prototype version of the interface system will be 
built ready for testing, first in laboratory environment and, after revaluation, in intended environment. 
T6.4 Control system components installation and testing . (M24-M30) Leader: IRIS Participants: UNED, 
UPCT, EXE, DRA, UPM  
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 51 
The control strategy defined in WP3, WP4, WP5 will be implemented in an embedded controller that will collect 
all measurements of sensors and apply control commands to all systems component and suitable. A specific 
electronic controller will be designed for the demonstrator ASTEP system by respecting the constraints of sensors 
integration, embedded computation, and external interface with computer to obtain an autonomous system to 
collect and monitor the performance of the system.  
T6.5 Test results integration (M24-M30) Leader: UPM Participants: UNED, UPCT, EXE, DRA 
This task is devoted to the integration of the results obtained in the previous tasks in a global model. UPM will 
lead the integration of the data obtained during the tests, where data of solar field tests will be provided by UPM 
and UNED, storage system data by UPCT whereas EXE and BUL will provide data from the ASTEP system. As 
a result of the model, an evaluation of the three sub-systems and their integration will be carried out. This analysis 
may prove that a sub-system model may need to be re-scaled for a more efficient integrated system, e.g. the ratio 
energy capacity/thermal power exchange of the storage s ystem may need to vary due to results obtained by the 
solar collector.  
T6.6 Revaluation of Designs of WP3 -WP4-WP5 After Testing -Validation (M24-M30) Leader: UNED 
Participants: UPM, UPCT, EXE, IRIS, DRA 
The basic design of the rotary Fresnel system , the storage system and the heat exchangers -absorption chiller will 
be checked and improved according to the test -validation task. In what refers to the solar concentrator , all the 
features of the systems (for both end -users) addressed in task s 3.1 and 3.2 will b e revaluated, considering the 
agreement between the testing results and the model’s prediction. The storage system tests will lead to a revaluation 
of the different phase change materials and structure and the compatibility with the needs of the chiller. In a second 
step, all the aspects learnt during the construction task and testing will be considered.  At this point, mitigation 
plans in case of eventual failures or contingencies will be implemented. Special attention will be put on the one - 
or two-axis tracking system that are key for the system, as well as the mirror mounting technique. Required changes 
on the three sub-systems will be done in order to optimize their performance at end-user sites. 
Role of Main partners: UPM will lead the ASTEP concept at Laboratory Environment assisted by UNED, UPCT, 
EXE, and ADSC.
