Objectives.  
The main objectives of this Work Package are: 
• Installation of the ASTEP units at the industrial sites (2 units). 
• Commissioning 
• Testing. 
• Monitoring and, finally, validation of the data obtained in the lab -trials based upon measurements made 
at the industrial sites. 
• Disseminating  the non-confidential data from the two Case Studies in a Report. 
Description of work 
The proposed work involves the integration of the ASTEP prototypes into the site -based industrial processes, 
involving (1) metal processing, and (2) dairy/cheese production , where they will be operated and monitored over 
a period of one year. 
Task 7.1 Implementation of Concept Design for 2 Test Cases (M30-M33). Leader: DRA 
Participants: See sub-tasks below 
• 7.1.1 (Metal processing) – AMTP, UNED, UPM, UPCT, IRIS, DRA 
For the AMTP site the ASTEP unit constructed and tested during WP6 will be dismantled and transported to 
the host company’s site. Any necessary troubleshooting will be undertaken, as will health and safety induction 
for both AMTP and visiting personnel. While it is anticipated that preparation work in WP6 will ease the path 
of the subsequent installation and commissioning, provision is allowed for changes in local conditions (such 
as production schedule) that might affect Task 7.2, part of which will run in parallel with the later stages of 
Task 7.1. Site weather conditions and solar insolation will be clarified during this stage. 
• 7.1.2 (Dairy/cheese production) – MAND, UNED, UPM, CRES, UPCT, IRIS, DRA 
The tasks here will be similar to those for Sub -task 7.1.1.  However, there will be an increased emphasis on 
ensuring that full hygiene procedures will be followed in commissioning etc., and also plann ing of the 
scheduling of the operation will be carefully studied to meet any changes in the production rota for the cheese 
etc. The addition of the absorption chiller will necessitate an extra emphasis on the scheduling and control 
aspects. 
Task 7.2 Installation & Commissioning on Site (M30-M33). Leader: DRA Participants: See sub-
tasks below. 
• 7.2.1 – AMTP, UPM, UNED, UPCT, IRIS, DRA 
AMTP engineers will assist the external team in assembling, installing and commissioning the solar thermal 
and storage system. Ideally this will be carried out during a process shut-down period, so that the control and 
storage systems can be tested without interference from or with the metallurgical processes. The performance 
of all components will be compared with those measured in laboratory testing and any anomalies addressed.  
This will be done on site where practicable. 
• 7.2.2 – MAND, UPM, UNED, CRES, UPCT, IRIS, DRA 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 53 
MAND scientists and engineers will assist the external team at this site. CRES will participate in the assembly 
and installation procedures of the solar system in the Greek industry and help in the positioning of the 
measuring equipment. The  commercially purchased absorption chiller will be integrated with the other 
components and included in the commissioning process. As in Sub -task 7.2.1, anomalies in behavior will be 
addressed. 
Task 7.3 Monitoring (M33-M45). Leader: DRA Participants: See sub-tasks below 
• 7.3.1 – AMTP, IRIS, RELA, EBOS 
• 7.3.2 – MAND, IRIS, CRES, EBOS 
This task will present all monitoring procedures carried out and results from the 2 Test Cases studies. The Task 
includes all the data from the measuring equipment, the various set ups tested together with data from the 
production process. The steel sector Test Case (AMTP) will be monitored by RELA while CRES will monitor the 
food sector Test Case (MAND) with special consideration of the absorption chiller unit. 
An important aspect of both monitoring exercises will be recording the maintenance needs – both preventative 
(e.g. keeping solar receivers clean) and addressing any breakdowns in the equipment, control system or other 
aspects of the installation. In both installations it will be important to ensure that the systems, should any failure 
occur, do not i nterfere with on -site metal or food production, and that a back -up system is available to ensure a 
smooth switch to normal operation should a failure occur. This task will include the development of an innovative 
dashboard by EBOS which will allow the collection of data from the various sensors and IoT gateways deployed 
at the lab sites. Using appropriate algorithms, analytics performance models will be created. All measurements and 
KPIs will be presented through a dashboard, using the latest state-of the-art web technologies, which will be able 
to remotely monitor in near real -time the various data collection points . CRES will gather the results from the 
Dairy industry (MAND), analyze the outcomes, and provide a comprehensive report detailing the system 
efficiencies. Similarly, RELA will gather similar results from the Steel industry (AMTP). 
Monitoring will extent over a one-year period to accommodate the four seasons. 
Task 7.4 Validation (M33-M45). Leader: DRA Participants: ADSC, UPM, UNED, UPCT EXE, 
BUL 
Validation exercises will be carried out based upon the data arising from both sites. This will involve comparisons 
of measured performance data with those obtained in laboratory trials. Of particular importance will be co -
ordination of plant performance data with the solar insolation during the trial period. A public report will be 
produced by DRA, bringing together data on the performance of both of the prototypes at the industrial sites. These 
will incorporate information on the LCA.  
The advanced intelligence dashboard developed by EBOS at T7.3 will be used for both understanding of the 
environment and for post data analytical purposes to assist in the validation exercises. The dashboard, supported 
by strong big data analytics mechanisms,  will enable the comparative assessment of the measurements performed 
against the expected KPIs, t hus supporting the WP actors to validate the  ASTEP concept and methodology, 
critically highlighting any relevant interference observed, gaps in the expected results, difficulties in the adaptation 
of the solution in the real use case, and other peculiarities of the context that might act as a constrain. 
Role of Main partners:  DRA will lead the ASTEP concept at the Industrial Environments assisted by UNED, 
CRES, RELA, EBOS, AMTP, and MAND.

Objectives.  
The main objectives of this work packages are: 
• To quantify and evaluate the effects to the environment caused by the manufacturing and using of the 
target heating/cooling modular system in industrial processes. 
• To determine the CapEx (Capital Expenditure) and OpEx (Operational Expenditure) at the different stages 
of the project and to guarantee cost -effectiveness and competitiveness of the target modular system  and 
forecast similar CapEx and OpEx analysis for the industrial version of the ASTEP 
• To identify and asse ss social aspects and overcome any possible related issues with the development of 
the target heating/cooling modular system.  
• To achieve a wide social acceptance by including all relevant stakeholders on the study and showing the 
advantages of implementing the target heating/cooling modular system in industrial processes. 
Description of work 
Task 8.1 Life Cycle Assessment (LCA). (M6-M46). Leader: VERT. Participants: EXE, BUL, UNED, 
UPCT, DRA, UPM, AMTP, MAND 
The present task will be focused on the assessment of the potential environmental impacts of ASTEP modular 
systems throughout their life cycle. The LCA analysis will involve the following stages: (i) definition of scope and 
goal, (ii) development of releva nt inventory inputs and outputs, (iii) assessment of their potential impacts and 
interpretation of results within the context of proposed targets. LCA will be carried out according to the guidelines 
of ISO 14040/14044. The environmental impact categories i nclude global warming potential, human toxicity, 
ecotoxicity, use of the resources, energy demand among others. Upon verification of the sensitivity and reliability 
of the study, relevant conclusions and recommendations will be created. The LCA will be per formed with the 
specialized software Simapro 8. The participation of technology developers and demonstrator´ managers will be 
required to provide information for the LCA Analysis. It is anticipated that the results of this study will demonstrate 
the positi ve environmental impacts of implementing the modular system for production of heating, cooling 
compared with similar heating/cooling systems at research stage too.  
Task 8.2 Life Cycle Costing (LCC) (M15-M46). Leader: BUL. Participants: VERT, EXE, UNED, UPCT, 
UPM, AMTP, MAND 
In this task the CapEx and OpEx costing for the use of the solar energy for generation of heating and cooling 
systems will be determined. They will be estimated on an annual basis and then related to the amount of generated 
energy divided by the expected amount of energy. A new decision support toolbox that covers all the aspects of 
the economic dimensions will be developed. It will cover two -way power flow and communications between 
various components . The toolbox will be able t o optimise several objective functions such as primary energy 
savings, emission reduction, minimum cost of CapEx and OpEx of the whole system.  It will be also used for 
determination of the indirect cost as productivity, costs of time, budget allocation an d compare the long -term 
expenses with the short -term expenses including CapEx. The developed model will then be used for the 
environmental and economic analysis of AMTP and MAND, respectively to find out the possible combinations of 
variables that will give the best performance concerning energy savings, emission reductions, and minimum cost 
of Renewable Energy Source (RES). 
Task 8.3 Social LCA. (M6-M46). Leader: VERT. Participants: EXE, BUL, UNED, UPCT, UPM 
Identify and assess social and socio-economic benefits of target modular system for production of heating, cooling 
and electricity. The Social LCA (S -LCA) methodology will be applied to evaluate the social impacts of 
implementing the target modular system in the project demonstrators and different impact  categories will be 
evaluated. The S-LCA is an innovative methodology that integrates traditional LCA methodological steps while 
having social impacts as focus. The basic steps of the LCA will be adopted also in S -LCA, namely: (1) defining 
goal and scope of the assessment; (2) inventory of the drivers which may lead to an impact; A life cycle inventory 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 55 
is elaborated for indicators (e.g. number of jobs created) linked to impact categories (e.g. local employment) which 
are related to five main stakeholder groups (e.g., [i] worker, [ii] consumer, [iii] local community, [iv] society and 
[v] value chain actors); (3) impact assessment based in the selection and calculation of proper indicators of impacts; 
and (4) interpretation of the results. The S -LCA methodolog y proposed embeds a detailed inventory method 
tailored on real data, collected directly from the field of application thanks to customized surveys that allow 
modelling the life cycle of the proposed technologies. S -LCA makes use of generic and site -specific data, can be 
quantitative, semi-quantitative or qualitative, and complements the environmental LCA and LCC. The envisaged 
positive results will constitute valuable inputs to stimulate preferences for these technologies and will be used as 
part of the bas eline information aimed to design an adequate strategy to increase stakeholders and consumers 
acceptance. 
Task 8.4 Social Acceptance. (M24-M46). Leader: VERT. Participants: BUL, ADSC, EBOS 
Specialized tools and methodologies such as Focus Groups Interviews , In-depth Interviews, Q -Sorts, Scenario 
Analysis, CO-creative workshops in order to involve the relevant stakeholders (e.g. user communities) from the 
early stages of the design and definition of Business Models will be realized, at local level, in each o f the 
demonstrators. As regards the focus groups, conceptualization (e.g. definition of population and samples) and 
logistics will be established, and skilled facilitators will encourage group interactions to capture relevant data and 
to provide a more com prehensive understanding of the group opinion. To recruit the participants for the focus 
groups the support of local agencies will be required. Several types of stakeholders will be involved, ranging from 
Public Authorities to community representatives. Ba sed on these results and sustainability assessments results, a 
strategy to improve Stakeholders’ acceptance and to engage a relevant number of stakeholders in the 
implementation of the target modular system will be realized. Gender balance will be considered. If gender-related 
differences are found in the acceptance of the proposed heating/cooling modular system these outcomes will be 
considered when preparing the strategy to increase social acceptance. Personal data collection will be limited to 
the data relevant for the research (i.e. age, education level). 
Task 8.5 Exergy Analysis (M6 – M42). Leader: EXE. Participants: BUL, UPM, UNED, UPCT 
An Exergy based simulation of different technology scenarios will be performed during this task. The simulations 
and optimization calculations will be based on the exergetic assessment of the mass and energy flux and will 
produce a comprehensive,  unbiased scientific rating that highlights the irreversibilities and inefficiencies within 
the ASTEP process.  The study will identify the efficiency of the whole system and of each individual component. 
Exergy assessment can define the steps of the process with the highest irreversibility and exergy destruction. This 
task will add a deeper view to improve the flexibility and optimization of the system and of each single component. 
In the first 20 months, a preliminary exergy study and optimization will be performed based on the available 
historical data or from theoretical assumption. This first analysis will be used to help define the best layout of the 
ASTEP technology. A first update of the exergy analysis will be performed in month 32 and month 42, the final 
study based on the data collected from WP6 and 7 will be carried out to verify, compare and propose additional 
improvements to the system. 
Role of Main partners: VERT will lead the Sustainability Assessment assisted by BUL, and EXE.

Objectives 
The main objectives of this work packages are: 
• To communicate, create awareness and promote ASTEP , to the public, scientific and industry 
community in the media. 
• To disseminate the outputs of research activities  from researchers, to industry/S MEs and 
policy/regulators, and ensure academic, industry and other relevant publications and to be present at 
conferences and other relevant activities as appropriate.  
• To create the Solar Energy Helix (virtual technology cluster/community hosted on the CH X’s Platform 
to accelerate the dissemination and exploitation plans and support in achieving ASTEP’s project and post 
project impact objectives. The Solar Energy Helix will support in networking across Europe and 
internationally (including the Mediterranean and MPC), working closely with all partners, particularly 
ADSC, DRA, UPCT, EBOS, BUL, CRES and IRIS, who have extensive international networks in this 
field, and linking ASTEP to oth er funded projects in this space, and bringing these networks and 
stakeholders into the Solar Energy Helix, in order to create a self-sustaining European/international cluster 
in solar energy for industrial processes.  
• To Develop an Exploitation Strategy t o ensure the protection of strategically important Intellectual 
Property, and a robust business plan to ensure post project impact and sustainability beyond the lifetime 
of the project. 
Description of work 
Task 9.1: Communication Strategy Activities (M1-M48). Leader: CHX, Participant: DRA, UPCT and All)  
Target audiences will be identified, ranging from researchers, solar energy companies, industries /SMEs and the 
public etc. in order to develop complementary communication and dissemination strategies. ASTEP will develop 
and implement a communication strategy by Month 6, raise the awareness with entities such as the IEA Solar 
Energy Programme, the Inte rnational Renewable Energy Association, Solar Heat Europe . To implement the 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 57 
communication strategy, we will set up a website and social media project accounts (i.e. Twitter, LinkedIn) , 
design and circulate leaflets and conference posters, and release press releases.  
The consortium website will be set up by the Coordinator, RELA, by Month 3. The website will serve as the 
primary contact point for external users and will include general information and updates on the progress made by 
ASTEP. The website will be divided into pages specifically focused on different end users (scienti sts, chemical 
energy, systems-catalysis and material engineering and manufacturing industries, and the public), and serve as a 
central hub for all communication to the wider public.  
Task 9.2: Dissemination Strategy Activities (M1-M48) Leader: UPCT, Participant: All)  
Target audiences will be identified ranging from researchers and industry/SMEs in solar energy and industrial 
processing especially in energy intensive sectors. UPCT will lead on generating a Dissemination Strategy, working 
in close collaboration with EXE, supported by all of the partners, who will lead on carrying out the dissemination 
activities. An important part of the Dissemination Strategy will be a timetable of  the dissemination activities, to 
ensure the protection of certain project results before being made public. Moreover, once the protection activities 
are concluded, UPCT will ensure that all internal dissemination has taken place before release of informat ion to 
the public. UPCT, ADSC, CHX, BUL, SUN, DRA, UNED, UPM , will consider  dissemination through all 
available media including, with focus on Solar Energy Helix to accelerate the disseminations strategy and 
results/information for dissemination through the Solar Energy Helix. 
The dissemination activities to actors who can leverage the produced results will include the publication of research 
papers in open-access journals such as Journal of Cleaner Production, Solar Energy, Renewable Energy, Thermal 
Science and Engineering Progress, and of papers jointly published with the industry, as well as the participation 
of consortium members in well-established conferences and workshops such as Eurotherm, HEFAT International 
Conference, ASME Power & Energy Conference, International Conference on Clean Energy and SolarPACES.. 
Task 9.3: Solar Energy Helix (M1-M48) Leader: CHX, Participant: All)  
CHX, working closely with partners, in particular  ADSC, DRA, EXE, CRES, UPCT, EBOS, BUL, IRIS, will 
create and manage a virtual cluster/community (Helix), called the Solar Energy Helix on the CHX platform that 
will act as the backbone of the dissemination and exploitation strategies developed in WP9 – for both during and 
after the project. As described in Section 2.2, The Crowdhelix (CHX) Network (https://network.crowdhelix.com/) 
has more than 400+ member organisations from 42 countries and is present in all EU Member State countries, 
from which there is an extended reach potential to more than 400 ,000 research and innovation actors. As CHX is 
set-up around thematic areas (Helixes), i.e. Energy, Climate, Manufacturing etc., and is supported by a technology 
platform where these virtual communities are hosted; CH X will create a new Helix for this proj ect. As CH X 
members have collectively won an estimated + 4 billion in funding from Horizon 2020, it will be able to easily 
connect with other funded projects from this call and previously funded projects in th ese areas (HYCOOL, 
SunHorizon, Innova-Microsolar) to bring them into the Helix. This will thereby leverage the EU’s investment into 
solar energy in industrial processes and decarbonisation, and facilitate knowledge sharing of results (open results) 
and connect all the projects to achieve a greater impact. The Solar Energy Helix will be set-up by Month 2, and 
profile >150 organisations (key stakeholders and end -users) by M24, including solar energy, and industrial 
processes and manufacturing industries and research actors, and participants of other funded H2020  projects 
and relevant actors across Europe/Interna tional. The organisations will be profiled in the following way: 1) 
People and Organizational Profiling ; 2) Knowledge and Expertise Profiling ; and 3) Projects in the area of 
solar energy and industrial processes (H2020, national and international). The organisations will be notified by 
the platform about the advancements of ASTEP project, with the aim of maximizing the visibility of results to 
actors best placed to make use of them, and broaden their impact enabling the creation of a community. CHX will 
work with in arranging three events, one per year, during the project, targeting key stakeholders to disseminate the 
results, and at the end of the project facilitate the exploitation/post project next steps (joint events with other funded 
projects in this sp ace will be considered, especially when targeting industry stakeholders). When launching and 
delivering the Solar Energy Helix , the following activities will take place: - In M2, launch Solar Energy Helix 
on the Crowdhelix Platform (design logo, launch sp ace on the platform, and communicate the new helix to the 
membership base); Profile >150 organisations (at researcher and organisational level) in the Crowdhelix platform 
(by M24); - Organise the first Helix event and launch/implementation of the its strat egy (M12); - Deliver impact 
in line with the Helix strategy (including supporting dissemination events, and building collaboration through the 
platform).  
Task 9.4: Exploitation strategy (M1-M48) Leader: EXE Participants: RELA, ADSC, EBOS, DRA, AMTP, 
MAND 
This task consists of the analysis of the project outcomes (technical innovations) with regard to their future 
exploitation possibilities along the different exploitation paths: 
• Transfer: enhance good practice by spreading results; 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 58 
• Commercialisation: creation of a new product or services or enhancement of existing ones; 
• Sustainability: keep project results visible and available for access of target audience. 
In order to continuously update and keep the focus on future exploitation, exploitation plans will be provided after 
each innovation cycle (midterm  and final exploitation plans). All partners are expected to actively plan their 
exploitation about future  market take-up. Detailed arrangements with respect to Intellectual Property Rights (IPR), 
access to partner owned knowledge and exploitation rules are settled by the Consortium Agreement which will be 
defined at the beginning of the project. IPR issues: exploitation of research results includes good preparation of 
IPR. It means that patents protect the results and that the results are exploited and are generating revenues for one 
or all partners of the projects. The IPR can be exploited by licensing the patent, selling the patent or if the patent 
is being used by the partners.   Exploitation activities will include: (i) Securing of intellectual property developed 
within the project, (ii) long term research and development strategy beyond the duration of the project and (iii) 
generation and implementation of an exploitation plan. The E xploitation Strategy will include the following 
elements: Main objectives and Responsibilities, Target groups and Key actors, Levels of exploitation and 
exploitable components, Communication channels and tools, to be coordinated with Task 8.1 and Task 8.2 from 
WP8. The first Exploitation strategy will be finalised at Month 24 and the final version will be prepared at the end 
of the project, to ensure a strategy that will be taken forward to take the results to the next phase following the end 
of the project. 
Role of Main partners: CHX will lead the Impact activities sharing tasks with UPCT, ADSC, EBOS, and EXE.

3.2 Management structure, milestones and procedures  
3.2.1 Organizational structure and decision making 
An organizational structure (see Fig. 3.3) with management procedures and decision -making mechanisms that are 
suitable for the scale of the project will be implemented to ensure the smooth implementation of the ASTEP project. 
The WP1 Project management and Coordination shall support the WPs, and the consortium partners. The General 
Assembly shall handle strategic and impact related decision -making. An Executive Board will be in charge of 
implementing the decisions. 
 
 
Figure 3.3: Organizational structure of the ASTEP project 
Project coordinator 
The Coordinator will be the intermediary between the partners and the EC and shall perform all tasks assigned to it as 
described in the Grant Agreement and the Consortium Agreement. As chairman of the General Assembly, 
responsibilities of the coordinator will include: 
• Monitor the compliance by the partners with their obligations, and that the project is implemented properly 
• Act as the intermediary for all communications between the partners and the EC 
• Request and review any documents or information required by the EC and verify their completeness and 
correctness before passing them on to the EC 
• Submit the deliverables and reports to the EC  
• Ensure that all payments are made to the other beneficiaries without unjustified delay 
• Inform the EC of the amounts paid to each partner, when required under the agreement or requested by the EC 
• Transmit documents and information connected with the project to any other partners concerned  
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 61 
Furthermore, the coordinator will take over the day -to-day management of the project consisting of both strategic 
(technical management, risks, external opportunities,) and operational (animation, communication, reporting) 
management tasks (see WP1 for details). 
The project coordinator will especially oversee: 
• Chairing the Executive Board  
• Organizing (methodologies, tools, knowledge management) and piloting at project level the S&T management 
carried out by the WP leaders on WP basis 
• Providing the General Assembly with critical analysis on the global technical performance of the pro ject 
especially through a close follow -up of the project level indicators (balanced scorecard) included in the 
dashboard as well as summarize related recommendations 
• Collecting and consolidating the deliverables reports and contributions for the progress a nd financial reports 
before review and validation by the Coordinator 
• Ensuring that the internal quality processes, common templates and communication tools decided by the 
General Assembly are properly used by the consortium members  
• Implementing the global risk management linked to milestones as detailed below 
• Ensuring on a daily basis the communication between the different partners (notably by implementing 
collaborative platform, being responsible for official meetings organizations) 
• Detecting project related needs and opportunities (whether it is scientific, networking or funding related)

Professor Antonio Rovira (M) , coordinator of the ASTEP, has experience in team management from 2011, both in 
academic staff and research project s. Ph.D. from Universidad Politécnica de Madrid since 2004, Lecturer since 2006 
(junior and senior) and Professor since 2019. From 2011 to 2014 was Pro-Vice-Chancellor of Infrastructures of UNED, 
coordinating the building move of four schools and the construction of a new building for the Science School. Currently 
is the Head of Department of the Energy Engineering Department. 
From 2011 is the Head of the STEAM research group. Prof. Rovira has been the principal researcher of SDCC (2006-
2008), InteCCSol (2012-2015) and HICCSA (2016-2019) projects, being the responsible of for the coordinated projects 
InteCCSol-CompoCCSol and HICCSA -DECCSA, and he has led several tasks of the EUROfusion resarch project 
(within WP22, 2017 -2019). He has also worked on five  additional projects related to the integration of solar energy 
within thermal systems, particularly thermodynamic power systems, both at national and European level during the 
last ten years (Advanced concepts of concentrating solar energy systems, ReConS ol, ACES2030, ConSOLI+Da and 
Futuro Solar). Also, he has translated its experience from other technologies related to thermal systems into the CSP 
field. He is co-author of roughly 50 contributions in international journals and 18 patents.  
General Assembly (GA) 
The GA is the ultimate decision making and conflict resolution body of the project. It will be chaired by the coordinator 
and attended by one representative of each partner. The GA will be responsible for the overall strategic orientation and 
policy of the project. It will make sure that the adopted strategy is respected in order to reach excellence. Its tasks 
include: 
• Assessment / agreement on project progress and resources status and allocations 
• Changes of Grant Agreement & technical annex to be submitted for EC approval 
• Changes to the work programme and its timing  
• Modifications to Consortium Agreement notably to Background Included, additions to list of Third Parties for 
simplified transfer, additions to Identified Affiliated Entities 
• Evolution of the consortium: conditions of entry & withdrawal of parties, identification of breach by a party or 
defaulting party 
• Agreeing on external opportunities 
• Ensuring the leverage effect of the project and achievement of expected impacts 
The General Assembly will meet physically at least every 6 months, exceptional sessions (telephone or web conference) 
may be called upon and organized when needed or requested. 
Executive Board (EB) 
Chaired by the Project Coordi nator, the Executive Board will be responsible for t he proper execution and 
implementation of the decisions of the General Assembly. It will monitor the effective and efficient implementation of 
the Project. Particularly, the EB will: 
• Collect information at least every 6 months on the progress, IPR, dissemi nation, communication etc. and 
resources status of the project 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019 
Page 62 
• Examine that information to assess the compliance of the project with the work plan and, if necessary, propose 
modifications to it to the General Assembly 
• Resolve conflicts on technical, financial and strategic issues and consult GA if needed 
• Agree on the members of the Management Support Team. 
• Support the Project Coordinator in preparing meetings with the EC and in preparing related data and 
deliverables 
• Prepare the content and timing of press releases and joint publications by the consortium or proposed by the 
EC 
• Propose and set up internal quality processes, common templates and communication tools

Monica Osorio is the Exploitation manager (F) has more than 15 years of experience in the market intelligence

Research & innovation activities reporting  
Technical and financial follow -up at the level of the whole project will be implemented on a 6 months basis and 
presented during General Assembly meetings who will assess the progress achieved by the project. Operational 
progress will be monitored by the Project Coordinator and WP leaders at the level of WP every 3 months. 
Physical meetings gathering the General Assembly will be organized on a 6-monthly basis in order to review and assess 
the project achievements. 
Project mid-term and final reviews will be implemented as stipulated in the Grant Agreement. The General Assembly 
will organize this mid-term meeting with all partners, and the EC if appropriate. The following criteria will be assessed: 
• Degree of fulfillment of the work plan for the relevant period and of the related deliverables 
• Continued relevance of the objectives and breakthrough potential with respect to the scientific and industrial 
state of the art 
• Resources planned and utilized in relation to the achieved progress, in a manner consistent with the principles 
of economy, efficiency and effectiveness 
• Management procedures and methods of the project 
• Partners’ contributions and integration within the project 
• Expected potential impact in economic, competition and social terms, and the partners' plan for the use and 
dissemination of results.

Decision making 
The GA will be the ultimate decision-making body for the project. The principles of the decision-making mechanisms 
to avoid status -quo or blocking situations, as described in the Consortium Agreement DESCA -H2020 under 
preparation, will be applied: 
• Each consortium body shall not deliberate and decide validly unless 2/3 of its members are present or 
represented (quorum). If the quorum is not reached, another meeting will be convened. 
• Each member present or represented shall have one vote (no vote for defaulting party) 
• Decisions shall be taken by a majority of 2/3 of the votes cast  
• From an operational point of view, the project will strive as follows for conflicts resolution:  
• Amicable solutions will be proposed for conflicted parties to find a compromise in an amicable and bilateral 
way; 
• If necessary, mediation will be conducted by the coordinator or an identified neutral party who will propose 
adequate timing for resolution; 
• Otherwise, rules of the Consortium Agreement (CA) will apply and decisions may be submitted to a vote; 
• In extreme cases, a clear risk assessment will be realize d and balance will be carefully weighed between the 
damages/solutions that can lead to defaulting partner exclusion. 
Important milestones have been identified for the project implementation and will be carefully monitored by the 
corresponding WP leaders, a nd at project level by the project coordinator. When the date of milestones review is 
achieved the results verification will be conducted against set objectives and a short report will be issued regarding the 
milestone’s assessment. When a milestone is del ayed or is not achieved, the impact on project course and WP will be 
assessed and a back -up plan will be proposed by the concerned WP leaders. Such issues will be reviewed by the EB 
who will report the milestones status to the GA.

Innovation management 
Innovation management involves different resources to successfully bring technologies generated from research 
activities to the markets. Such process requires a strong interlink between Research & Innovation activities, Intellectual 
Property Rights management and Exploitation management that are covered in the project, especially: 
• Results identification and recognition of intellectual property (IP) will be under the responsibility of the 
Exploitation & Innovation as well as IPR manager 
• IP assessment and protection will be under responsibility of the IPR manager 
• For all identified and exploitable IP, exploitation and business plans will be developed under the responsibility 
of the Exploitation & Innovation 
Identification and monitoring of such innovation related issues will be reviewed during EB sessions. The EB will report 
to the GA that will decide the innovation management policies to be implemented for the project in accordance to the 
Consortium Agreement rules (see Fig. 3.3)

accordance to the Consortium Agreement rules (see Fig. 3.4)

3.3 Consortium as a whole  
The consortium consists of 17 partners including 1 RTO, 6 universities together with 8 SMEs and 2 Industrial 
Corporations; linking technology providers and RTO with end users, initially represented by the three trial houses. The 
consortium has well-balanced skill sets from 9 different member states with a balanced geographical distribution across 
Europe with SME representing a very important part of the industrial partners, 47% of the whole consortium. 
The partners have been selected from the leading groups in Europe to have complementary technical capabilities, 
infrastructure and know-how to reach the ambitious technological goals of the project. This represents the leading-edge 
nature of this field, which has yet to obtain significant traction amongst LEs. Consequently, the consortium assembled 
represents the state-of-the-art with regard to solar thermal energy and storage and advanced process integration  (Fig. 
3.5), and hence as a whole is the best-placed consortium to deliver the planned technological innovation. This reflects 
the current status of use of low-grade energy streams, in that the developments anticipated within this project represent 
enabling technologies for growth in  the importance of the technology and hence the size of the industrial companies 
involved. 
This proposal version was submitted by Antonio ROVIRA on 27/08/2019 13:57:53 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
  LC-RES-07-2019

In addition, the consortium has the capability to credibly exploit the project results both in short -term and in making 
plans for the long -term. Most of the partners ,  not only RTO and ACA but also SMEs, have already collaborated in 
other European projects and have thus shown their capability of efficient project collaboration  and in effectively 
generating, protecting and exploiting IP. The capabilities of the different partners are well equilibrated to complement 
each other in all major activities that ensures that there is no unnecessary overlap of activities as clarified in the WP 
descriptions. The effort of the consortium partners has been allocated to the tasks wi thin the different WPs based on 
their expertise and technical capabilities, as detailed in Section 3.4, 8 partners have also been appointed WP leaders, as 
shown in Table 3.2, based on their skills and experience. Each partner plays a unique role in the pro ject and provides 
technical support and assistance for other partners. 
The coordination of the project is ensured by Dr Antonio Rovira which has experience in leading large-scale European 
collaborative projects. In the area of securing maximum exploitation , the Partners will be assisted by Monica Osorio 
the Exploitation Manager (Section 3.2.1). The core skill sets and roles in the different European funded   project are 
shown in section 4-5.

Section 4: Members of the consortium 
4.1. Participants 
The consortium has been carefully selected to enable the achievement of the objectives set in cross -cutting call 
“Building a Low -carbon, climate resilient future ” for Topic  LC-RES-07-2019 “Solar Energy in Industrial 
Processes”. O perational capacities, knowledge and experience of the project partners (described below for each 
partner) are on top-level in Europe, which ensures efficient exploitation and impact of the project. 
 
Partner 1: UNIVERSIDAD NACIONAL EDUCACION A DISTANCIA, PIC: 999863294 
Short Name UNED Country Spain 
 
Type ACA Website www.uned.es 
Brief description of the organisation 
The UNED-STEM (Thermal Systems, Energy and Environment) research group was created in 2007, within 
the Energy Engineering Department at UNED (National Distance Education University, Madrid, Spain). 
This group has focused its investigations in the fields of optimisation and management of thermal and 
thermoelectric systems, in particular, sol ar thermal plants. The main research lines of the group are the 
following: 
▪ Analysis and simulation of Concentrating Solar Power Plants (CSPP): optics, receivers, storage 
systems and power blocks. 
▪ Thermodynamic and thermoeconomic optimization of combined cycles: conventional technologies 
(CCGT) and hybrid technologies with solar integration (ISCC). 
▪ Design, simulation and development of absorption chillers for the production of solar cooling in 
buildings; solar heating systems with flat plate collectors of high efficiency. 
▪ Energy efficiency and emissions reduction in buildings: analysis and modeling of heat bridges in 
buildings; simulation and analysis of the components in thermal installations; energy and environmental 
certification in the buildings. 
The UNED-STEM group has an extensive experience in the Fresnel collector technology. The group has 
participated, together with the UPM (Polytechnic University of Madrid), in the project "Concentrated Solar 
Power for Electricity Generation" (2012 -2013), granted by  the German Ministry: Bundesministerium für 
Bildung und Forshung. More recently, the research group has participated in the Future Solar project, with 
the UPM and the OHL company, which consists of the design and construction of an advanced Fresnel 
prototype in the UPM technological campus. 
Role in the project 
UNED will be the coordinating entity from the consortium as they will be the leader of WP1. They will 
apply its knowledge and expertise on solar systems as leader of WP3. Additionally, they will also collaborate 
in WP1, WP2, WP4, WP5, WP6, WP7  with other consortium partners. UNED will provide information 
for the sustainability assessment in WP8. Finally, U NED will also collaborate in communication, 
exploitation and dissemination activities in WP9. 
Key personnel 
• Professor Antonio Rovira (M) , coordinator of ASTEP  proposal, has experience in team 
management from 2011, both in academic staff and research projects. Ph.D. from Universidad 
Politécnica de Madrid since 2004, Lecturer since 2006 (junior and senior) and Professor since 2019. 
From 2011 to 2014 was Pro -Vice-Chancellor of Infrastructures of UNED, coordinating the building 
move of four schools and the construction of a new building for the Science School. Currently is the 
Head of Department of the Energy Engineering Department. 
From 2011 is the Head of the STEAM research group. Prof. Rovira has been the principal researcher of 
SDCC (2006-2008), InteCCSol (2012-2015) and HICCSA (2016-2019) projects, being the responsible 
of for the coordinated projects InteCCSol -CompoCCSol and HICCSA -DECCSA, and he has lead 
several tasks of the EUROfusion resarch project (within WP22, 2017-2019). He has also worked on five 
additional projects related to the integration of solar energy within thermal systems, particularly

• Dr. María José Montes (F) Ph.D. from Universidad Politécnica de Madrid. She is Associate Professor

(including solar plants), as well as in the global operation of these facilities. She has a wide experience 
in simulation studies and optimization of thermodynamic processes to increase the efficiency of 
different thermal facilities. The tools used to carry out the mentioned studies have been Matlab and EES,

international projects focused on thermal systems and solar energy.

Professor at UNED University. His main research topic has been the modelling, simulation and 
development of new solar cooling absorption prototypes with which he obtained his PhD and the 
mention of "Doctor Europeus". He made research stays in the “Solar Energy Lab” at the University of 
Wisconsin-Madison with Professor Sanford Klein and at the Delft University of Technology with 
Professor Carlos Infante Ferreira. He has participated in several national research projects related to the 
solar heating and cooling, highlighting: SIMUFRISOL (where he was the Principal Investigator), on the 
development of a high efficiency absorption chiller prototype for solar cooling and trigeneration; 
INVISO, on the theoretical and experimental evaluation of a solar heating and cooling prototype for the 
generation of sustainable energy in buildings. He has actively participated in Task 38 and Task 45 of 
the International Energy Agency (IEA) by publishing a chapter in the Handbook on Solar Cooling 
Systems. He has published 17 articles in international journals of the JCR and 33 works in international 
conferences. He is also a reviewer of 6 indexed international journals. 
• Dr. Fernando Varela (M) , Ph.D. from Universid ad de Valladolid, is an Associate Professor in the 
School of Engineering, in the area of Thermodynamics, at UNED. He holds his Bachelor in Mechanical 
Engineering, MSc. in Mathematics and Ph.D. in Industrial Engineering. He is currently His main 
research fields are building physics and energy systems, and CSP plants. He is co -author of 14 JCR 
articles and 25 contributions in international congresses. Dr. Varela has been also working in software 
development for Saunier Duval, energy monitoring for Daikin, training for UPONOR, and LEED 
certification for INDRA. 
• Dr. Marta Muñoz (F)  ), Ph.D. from UNED,  is an Associate Professor in the Energy Engineering 
Department at UNED University, belongs to the UNED -STEM research group since its formation, 
taking part in various of the current research projects. Her research activity began in the field of 
reciprocating thermal engines (PhD Thesis), but nowadays she is centered in the simulation of thermal 
processes, namely, power plants with solar energy hybridization and design and off-design performance 
of thermal equipment.

Previous projects / activities related to the subject of this proposal 
• "Solar concentrating thermal power in the transport sector and the int heat/electricity production 
(ACES2030)". P2018/EMT-4319.. Several Universities and technological centers (CIEMAT, IMDEA and 
CSIC) participate in this project. As the name suggests, the project covers the three main areas of application 
of concentrated solar energy: transport, heat and electricity production. The UNED group is responsible for 
the development of supercritical CO2 cycles and the development of Fresnel technology applied to process 
heat. From 01/01/2019 – 31/12/2022 
• “Advaced Integrated Solar Combined Cycles . (HICCSA)”. Spanish National Project. ENE2015-
70515-C2-1-R. This project has been coordinated by UNED and UPM Universities. The project has been 
focused in the integration schemes, as well as in the thermal simulation of the different components, in 
particular, all t he components in the solar subsystem, in which the three main technologies are included: 
Parabolic Trough Collectors, Central Receiver and Fresnel Collectors. From 01/01/2016 – 31/12/2019. 
• “Futuro Solar” This project was accomplished by UNED, UPM and OHL company. The main 
objective of the project was the design, the optimization and the construction of a Fresnel Collector 
Prototype. The main task for the UNED group was the thermo-fluid dynamic design of the Fresnel Receiver. 
The group also participated in the optical design. As a result of all these studies, UPM and UNED presented 
several patents, most of them extended to an international level. From 1/8/2014 to 31/12/2015. 
• “Technological investigation and thermo -economic optimization of Integrated Solar 
Combined Cycles (InTecSol) ”. Spanish National Project ENE2012-37950-C02-01 This project, also 
coordinated by UNED and UPM, is previous to HICCSA project, and it is also focused on thermal systems 
and thermal components, included the solar field. From 01/02/2013 to 01/01/2016. 
• “Concentrated Solar Power for Electricity Generation”. Project granted by the German Ministry:  
Bundesministerium für Bildung und Forshung  . This project was accomplished by the IASS (Institute for 
Advanced Sustainability Studies), UPM and UNED University. The UNED contributed in the development 
of a program for the optical characterization of a Fresnel Collector using the ray tracing and Monte Carlo 
methods. From 01/02/2012 to 01/01/2013.

Brief description of the organisation 
The company is known commercially as ANALISIS -DSC is a SME engineering company specialized in 
mechanical engineering and process engineering in applications related to fluid mechanics, heat transfer, 
bulk materials using CAE tools such as CFD, FEA, etc.  
The company was founded in the year 2002 in Madrid, Spain. The company has a high specialization in the 
analysis of complex industrial processes involving fluids in tasks of: 
• Basic Engineering, 
• Failure Engineering, 
• Analysis, Optimization and Scale-up of Industrial Processes. 
ANALISIS-DSC usually works for customers in the Iberian Peninsula and subcontracted to other 
international customers which might need our specialized engineering services when they face operational 
or design problems. ANALISIS -DSC is a h orizontal engineering company with references in most of the 
main economic sectors such as Naval, Energy, Civil, Hydraulics, Chemistry, etc 
Role in the project 
ADSC will collaborate in the general coordination of the project in WP1. ADSC will mainly perform tasks 
of thermomechanical analysis of the SunDial in WP3, charge -discharge analysis of the thermal storage in 
WP4 using CAE tools such as CFD  in WP2. ADSC will also participate in the revision of the developed 
models in WP6. ADSC will collaborate in the validation of the models in WP7. ADSC will collaborate in 
general sustainability tasks in WP8. Finally, ADSC will collaborate in general dissemination and 
exploitation tasks in WP9.

Partner 4: UNIVERSIDAD POLITECNICA DE CARTAGENA, PIC: 999828859 
Short Name UPCT  Country Spain 
 
Type ACA Website www.upct.es 
Brief description of the organisation 
UPCT (Universidad Politécnica de Cartagena) is a public University committed to the promotion of R&D, 
innovation and scientific exchange with numerous public and private, national and international institutions, 
reinforcing its links with industry. With ov er 90 R&D groups, UPCT seeks knowledge dissemination and 
scientific/technological creation.  
The Research Group of Fluid Mechanics and Thermal Engineering was founded in 1999 at UPCT. The 
host research expertise involves the development and application of experimental and modelling methods 
to provide satisfactory solutions to practical thermo -fluid problems. The research activity carried out is 
focused on: heat transfer enhancement, design and analysis of thermo-fluid systems, renewable energy and 
HVAC syst ems. The research group has gained international reputation in the field of heat transfer 
enhancement. Public funds and industrial sponsors have extensively supported our research. 
The UPCT has a supporting office, the OPECT, which vast experience on European project management. It 
possesses an active communication channel ensuring a proper project progress and report of project 
development, including administrative and financial aspects on costs related to the action.  The European 
Projects Office of UPCT has a wide experience in EU and international projects. Since its creation in 2009 
we have applied for more than 180 projects in different European calls. Currently, the office is managing 14 
European projects, in major programs, such as Horizon 2020, Directorate General, Erasmus+, Interreg Med 
and Sudoe, PRIMA, etc. 
Furthermore, the IPR Office at the UPCT facilitates and promotes collaboration between the world of 
university research and the companies in its socio-economic environment. It has the following functions: 
• Identification, evaluation, protection, dissemination and promotion of the knowledge and skills 
generated within the UPCT, promoting technology transfer 
• Promotion, participation and advice in the preparation and negotiation of research agre ements and in 
the preparation of project proposals. 
Role in the project 
The UPCT team will have an active role to undertake WP5. Furthermore, UPCT will take an active and 
supportive role in relevant tasks of the other work packages based on its technical and scientific background. 
UPCT EU project office will help the coordinat or with administrative tasks, financial reporting, research 
and legal advising and any other relevant issues that may appears throughout the project period. UPCT will 
also participate in WP8, following the long -term experience of the participating members in sustainability 
assessment for energy production and conservation. This partner will be the leader of WP5. 
Key personnel 
• Dr. Juan Pedro Solano (M) is an Associate Professor in Thermal Engineering at UPCT. His research 
interests cover the experimental and numerical analysis of enhanced heat transfer technologies of and 
thermal energy storage.  During the last years, he has applied his expertise analysis of active heat transfer 
enhancement techniques, with applications to mechanically-activated heat exchangers, oscillatory flow 
reactors and also to the development of novel designs of enhanced flat -plate solar collectors. He is

Brief description of the organisation 
David Reay & Associates (DRA) was set up early in 1987 as a consulting engineering organisation with an 
emphasis on energy technologies. It currently operates as a 'sole trader' with David Reay as Principal 
Consultant. While DRA has had Associates for many years, including Professor Colin Ramshaw, regarded 
as the ‘father’ of process intensification, in 2012 it was decided, because of increasingly close involvements 
with areas such as process intensification, compact heat exchangers and energy storage, to expand the 
organisation by bringing in three additional Associates, all highly qualified for this project.  They 
complement the activities of Professor Colin Ramshaw, who has been an Associate for many years. DRA 
was a major player in the IbD SPIRE Project, that provides significant input/tools to our current proposal. 
DRA also took over some Management roles in IbD from other partners 
Role in the project 
DRA will act as scientific and innovation managers, will assume a scientific co -ordination role. DRA will 
participate in WP3 and WP4 and assist in WP9 on Dissemination. This partner will be the leader of WP7.

blend easily with the customer’s existing infrastructure, allowing them at the same time to work with tools

minimising their learning curve.

Partner 8: BRUNEL UNIVERSITY LONDON, PIC: 999749610 
Short Name BUL Country United Kingdom 
 
Type ACA Website www.brunel.ac.uk 
Brief description of the organisation 
Brunel University London (BUL) in West London is a dynamic institution with over 12,500 students and 
over 1,300 academic staff operating in a vibrant culture of research excellence.  With a turnover of more 
than £200 million, the University is a Higher Education and research establishm ent with considerable 
intellectual, financial and social resources and makes a major contribution to the economy and community 
of the West London region. It also plays a significant role in the higher education scene nationally and has 
numerous national an d international links and partnerships with both academia and industry. BUL has 
climbed 14 places in the 2019 QS World University Rankings , and is now placed in the top third of 
universities worldwide.  Brunel prides itself on its multicultural environment and has gained countless 
benefits from having staff and students from over 113 different countries contributing to both its academic 
and social environment. The university holds a European Commission HR Excellence in Research award 
for its commitment to supporting its researchers.  
BUL has a long history of successful bidding for European funding and of managing EU projects, BUL was 
involved in 120 projects within FP7 with a cumulative value of over 37 Million Euros, and has been 
successful with over 60 Horizon 2020 proposals to the value of 30 million Euros, of which it is leading and 
coordinating 9 projects. 
Since the launch of the university in 1966, research has been at the very heart of Brunel's academic 
activities. Today, we have three Research Institu te’s covering most of these areas. The research groups 
within them are world leading, with highly cited papers, substantial grant income, established reputations 
for particular methodological approaches, and a community of PhD graduates pursuing successful  careers 
in industry and academia;  
The Institute of Energy Futures (IEF) is one of the institutes at BUL with a holistic approach to the energy 
costs of food distribution, bringing together researchers from a range of disciplines, as well as mainstream 
engineering research. It has a particular strength in refrigeration, heating and cooling and in environmental 
design. The Institute main themes include Advanced Powertrains and Fuels, Energy Efficient and 
Sustainable Technologies, Smart Power Networks and Re source Efficient Future Cities.  The Centre for 
Sustainable Energy Use in Food Chains is part of the IEF and is one of the 6 Centres funded by the 
Research Councils, UK to address 'End Use Energy Demand Reduction' in the UK. The Centre with an 
additional £5.0 m from BUL has established state of the art facilities for resource use reduction across all 
stages of the food chain. These include energy efficient food storage, transport, preservation and 
manufacturing technologies, and the use of low carbon energy in food processing. 
Role in the project 
BUL will coordinate WP2. BUL will be also involved in LCC analysis in WP8. Finally, BUL will also 
collaborate in general coordination tasks in WP1 and different activities in dissemination, exploitation 
communication in WP9.

Partner 9: CROWDHELIX LIMITED, PIC: 905205165 
Short Name CHX Country Ireland 
 
Type SME Website www.network.crowdhelix.com/  
Brief description of the organisation 
Vision2020: The Crowdhelix Network (CH) is a pan -European Open Innovation Network that enables 
Research Technology Organisations (RTOs) and businesses to collaborate, innovate and grow. Based at the 
Tyndall National Institute at University College Cork, the Crowdhelix Network has more than 400+ member 
organisations from 42 countries and is present in all EU Member State countries. The network membership 
is reported to have won more than 2.5 billion euros of funding under Horizon 2020, highlighting the quality 
of its membership base.  
The network is structured around virtual technology clusters known as Helixes. There are currently 18 live 
Helixes in areas such as Digital, Health and Energy etc. The network hosts focused collaborative events for 
each Helix ea ch year where the aim is to connect organisations across Europe and promote collaboration 
and open innovation. In addition to hosting and running events, CH also has its own technology tool called: 
Crowdhelix. The tool is designed so people and organisatio ns can profile their expertise and capabilities 
within a Helix area. It is then used to help organisations post opportunities, which are matched to people’s 
profiles within the platform. Once a match is made the CH team then help to facilitate an opportunity so that 
it then turns into a tangible collaboration. 
Role in the project 
CHX will set up a bespoke technology cluster ( Helix) for the project,  in turn acting as a commercial 
accelerator for the project with the principal goal of driving sustained indu stry exploitation, identifying IP 
licencing opportunities for continued revenues, motivating commercial partnerships, and steering industry 
& economic sustainability paths. The Helix will include all project partners, as well as relevant stakeholders 
from the pan-European CH community that currently has a reach to over 500,000 actors across 42 European 
countries (EU SMEs, RTOs, Universities and Industries). More fundamentally, the Helix will profile and 
inject relevant commercial actors from across Europe, such as SMEs and Industry leaders commercialising 
in this space, with a view to forging alliances and partnerships that are in the spirit of growth, expansion and 
ongoing sustainability and advancement of the IP created beyond the end of the project. The project’s Helix 
will also integrate other aligned projects in the domain of the project, with the end goal of establishing and 
motivating commercial partnerships across domain relevant sister -projects in this space, thus fusing and 
joining relevant actors on a path towards realising commercial outputs through commercial partnerships that 
the Helix will identify and motivate.  
The Helix will also identify relevant and appropriate open source communities with a view to ensuring that 
open outputs from the project are made available and accessible to all EU SMEs, RTOs, Universities and 
Industry actors, in the spirit of open dissemination and sharing.  
CHX will play a central role in enabling and supporting commercialisation and Industry adoption of the IP 
created, with appropriate outreach activities channelled and driven through the Helix. The project’s 
commercialisation, exploitation and IP strategy will be part of, and integrated into, the Helix activities and 
the Helix will also help to form and drive new forms of untapped capability and capacity in this area. The 
Helix will act as a commercial and economic accelerator for the project both during the project and after the 
project has ended. CHX will continue to manage the community beyond the end of the project – promoting 
the project’s outputs and impacts and enabling new forms of collaboration and open innovation across the 
European Research Area.

Short Name  RELA  Country Greece 
 Type SME Website www.relationalfs.com 
Brief description of the organisation 
Founded in Athens, Greece in 1995, Relational Technology SA has evolved over the years from one of the 
most promising independent software vendors in Greece, to an International Software Developer & Integrator 
with international presence and offices in Romania, Croatia, UK and a client base all over Europe, Middle 
East and North Africa. Its strategy supports strongly its expansion to markets outside Greece with current 
intense marketing activities in Europe (especial ly Balkans), Middle East and North Africa. Relational 
Technology SA has an average annual revenue of € 12.000.000 the last three years and employs an average 
of 130 persons. 
In addition, Relational provides system services relating to the following: 
• Project Management : Relational’s project management services undertake the task of planning, 
organizing, securing, and managing resources to achieve a project’s specific goals and to bring added 
value to the end result.  
• Business Process Reengineering (BPR): is defined as the fundamental rethinking and radical redesign 
of business processes to achieve dramatic improvements in critical contemporary measures of 
performance such as cost, quality and speed. BPR aims to make the structure of an organization serve 
the flow of products/services and result in the production of leaner and fitter organizations. 
• Software Development : actively participates in a number of European Community and National 
Research Projects with emphasis on intelligent data explo itation techniques defining and 
implementing efficient algorithms on data representation. 
• Anti-Fraud Management: experience and know-how as well as the technical competence required to 
effectively manage the anti-fraud lifecycle. 
Over the last 20 years, Relational Technology SA has worked extensively on many relevant aspects related 
to electricity, gas, oil, coal, renewable energy, energy efficiency and sustainable development for both EU 
and non EU Mediterranean countries. Relational Technology SA has a lo ng-standing experience in 
coordinating research projects on energy including renewable energy in the Euro -Mediterranean area with a 
large number of partners and in organising conferences for the dissemination of the research results for 
various stakeholders, including the European Commission, the World Bank, the International Energy Agency. 
Overall, it has been partner or coordinator of about 30 EU research projects. In addition, Relational 
Technology SA closely cooperates with a large network of experts in industry, universities, ministries, energy 
agencies, international organizations. Relational Technology SA is also partner of the Mediterranean 
Renewable Energy Programme, the Type II Initiative launched by the Italian government in 2002 and is also 
collaborating with the Secretariat of the UfM and Medgrid, under the framework of different memoranda of 
understanding. Its staff is composed of experienced engineers and economists from various Mediterranean 
countries, with solid analytical background on energ y scenario modeling, policy and market analysis. The 
organization is structured around four main fields of work: Hydrocarbons, Electricity, Renewable Energy, 
Monitoring and Modeling. The Technical Committees of Relational Technology SA , decide on priority 
projects, activities or studies to undertake, bring together representatives from members and external partners 
and regional stakeholders. 
Relational Technology SA is certified with the international quality standard EN ISO 9001, since May 2003, 
thus consolidating its philosophy for quality services, continuous improvement and increasing satisfaction 
for both of its customers worldwide and its partners, at all levels. Having placed Quality on the top of its 
strategic orientations, acknowledging that it is the most essential factor that provides the competitive edge in 
all services, Relational has developed and implements a certified - Quality Management System. This Quality 
Management System was planned and developed in conjunction with all the critical mana gement functions 
as reflected in the documented procedures and guidelines. The ISO 9001certification demonstrates that its 
Quality Management System is comprehensive and in accordance to the internationally accepted quality

• PIXEL Ports are a great example of heterogeneous information hubs. Multiple stakeholders operate 
inside and outside them with different motivations and businesses. Although document and dat a 
interchange are already in place through Port Community Systems (PCS), the interchange is limited to 
official documentation and services of the Port Authority, such as custom declarations, import/export of 
cargo, and other formal documents. However, an e ffective integration of operational data is far from 
optimal in most ports, and especially so in medium or small ports, where budget is limited and IT services 
usually is outsourced. PIXEL will enable a two -way collaboration of ports, multimodal transport agents 
and cities for optimal use of internal and external resources, sustainable economic growth and 
environmental impact mitigation, towards the Ports of the Future. PIXEL will leverage technological 
enablers to voluntary exchange data among ports and stakeholders, thus ensuring a measurable benefit in 
this process. The main outcome of this technology will be efficient use of resources in ports, sustainable 
development and green growth of ports and surrounding cities/regions.

sensing services for emerging smart cities’. RADICAL will enable the development and deployment of 
interoperable pervasive multi-sensory and socially-aware services, by leveraging Internet of Things (IoT) 
and Social Network (SN) technologies, emerging from leading edge R&D results from the 
SmartSantander, BonFIRE, SocIoS, and +Spaces projects. The RADICAL platform will also facilitate 
smart governance and flexible replication of services across cities and regions, through mechanisms that 
assess the cities’ peculiarities in terms both of their technical infrastructures and of the socio-economical 
characteristics and the legal and governance environments. RADICAL will integrate, deploy and pilot 
seven services in the areas of Cycling Safety, Green Products Management, Data Journalism, 
Participatory Urbanism, Augmented Reality, Eco-consciousness and Commercial and transactional data 
for pedestrian flows. http://www.radical-project.eu/ 
• ECIM [EU]: ‘European Cloud marketplace for Intelligent Mobility’: ECIM will 1) provide a pathway 
for cities and businesses to easily migrate services to the cloud, 2) open these services to innovators for 
use as the basis for new applications and services and 3) lever age existing CIP Marketplaces for 
Intelligent City (EPIC & EnoLL) services to promote new services across Europe. The EPIC marketplace 
features a secure and sustainable Platform as a Service (PaaS) that enables SMEs from across Europe to 
sell their web services and applications to Public Authorities. Pilot sites in Barcelona, Spain, Paris, France 
and Brussels, Belgium and a proof of concept in Birmingham region (UK) will validate the ECIM 
solution by 1) submitting existing services 2) engaging citizens and SMEs to co-create new services and 
3) implementing new ECIM services in their own areas. Pilots will upload and share new services 
between themselves to demonstrate the robust, cross border interoperability of the solution. ECIM has 
selected mobility and parking as a validation scenario because these services can easily be migrated to a 
cloud infrastructure and are consistently cited as high priorities for citizens and public service providers 
alike. (2012-2015) www.ecim-cities.eu/

Partner 11: UNIVERSIDAD POLITÉCNICA DE MADRID, PIC: 999974844 
Short Name UPM Country Spain 
 
Type ACA Website ww.upm.es 
Brief description of the organisation 
Universidad Politécnica de Madrid (UPM) is the largest Spanish technological university specialized in all 
engineering fields and architecture. With two recognitions as Campus of International Excellence, its 
outstanding research activity together with its highly qualified professional trainings, make UPM a really 
competitive university at international level. More than 2.400 researchers carry out their activity at the UPM, 
grouped in more than 200 Research Groups, 20 Research Centers or Institutes and 55 Laboratories, all of 
them committed to transform the knowledge generated into innovation advances applied to the productive 
sector, contributing to solve the challenges of the European citizens. 
The intense collaboration with governmental bodies and industry guarantees that research at UPM offers 
real solutions to real -world problems. The dyna mism of R&D&I activity at the UPM, together with the 
transfer of knowledge to society, are among its lines of strategy.  
These two commitments place UPM among the Spanish universities with the greatest research activity, both 
at national and international level, counting on an International Project Office that helps and support 
researchers in the international research arena. UPM highly innovation driven commitment is showed by 
the application for around 40 patents/year thanks to its Technology Transfer Off ice and by the generation 
around 20 spinoff/year (70% survival rate) trained and mentored by the UPM Center for Innovation Support. 
Moreover, UPM is highly committed to communication and outreach with and specific unit devoted to it. 
All this shows that UPM is an institution committed to the transfer of knowledge generated through its 
research structures to society, and its transformation into advances and technological developments applied 
to the productive sector. 
UPM-GIT (Universidad Politécnica d e Madrid – Thermoenergetic Research Group) was created in 2006, 
when it was focused on modeling of thermal energy systems, both renewables and nuclear.  Since then its 
activity has been growing yearly, especially in the field of concentrating solar power.  
The main research lines of the group are the following: 
• Design and optimization of concentrating solar power plants: optics, receiver, storage, etc. 
• Analysis and simulation of innovative power cycles. 
• Design of turbomachinery for ORC. 
• CFD simulation: solar receivers and turbomachinery. 
• Design of superconductor refrigeration systems. 
The intensive activity of UPM -GIT in several national and international projects has led to more than 50 
patents and 100 published articles. This includes the p articipation in a  project ended in the design, 
construction and test of a trough collector loop cooled by CO 2 at high temperature (500ºC) and pressure 
(100 bar) with CIEMAT at Plataforma Solar de Almería, and project  "Concentrated Solar Power for 
Electricity Generation" (2012 -2013), granted by the German Ministry: Bundesministerium für Bildung und 
Forshung. More recently, the research group has participated in Futur o Solar project, with STEM-UNED 
and OHL company, which consists on the design and construction of an advanced Fresnel prototype in the 
UPM technological campus.  In addition, UPM -GIT has participated in the FP7 project named BEST 
PAHTS, coordinated by Red Eléctrica de España with a total budget of 62.8 M€ for the development of 
HVDC corridors 
Role in the project 
UPM is the leader of WP6 with the expertise on solar collectors and solar systems in general. Additional, 
UPM also collaborates in WP2, WP3, WP4, WP5, WP7  and WP8. Finally, UPM will collaborate in 
different activities for exploitation, and dissemination and communication activities in WP9.

Partner 12: ARCELOR MITTAL TUBULAR PRODUCTS IASI, PIC: 898938868 
Short Name AMTP Country Romania 
 
Type IND Website http://tubular.arcel
ormittal.com 
Brief description of the organisation 
AM Iasi belongs to ArcelorMittal Tubular Products – AMTP – Europe Division within ArcelorMittal, the 
world’s leading steel and mining company. 
In particular, AM Iasi is engaged with the manufacturing of welded steel tubes for many diverse applications. 
Their main products are: 
• hollow sections for structural purposes 
• pipes for the conveyance of fluids  
• tubes for mechanical applications 
• tubes for automotive applications (they are starting in this sector) 
The main manufacturing process used in the plant is the cold-forming of the tubes, through which a steel 
slitting coil used as raw material is formed into a rounded shape in a continuous forming process for a 
subsequent welding operation where both edges of the steel band are joined together obtaining a cir cular 
tubular section. In some occasions, the weld seam can be in -line heat-treated by a seam annealing process. 
In any case, this circular tube is then passed through a set of sizing rolls for getting the final cross -section 
of the tube (can be circular, square, rectangular, oval…) and it is cut to the required length. 
Finally, depending on the final use of the product, the extremes of the tubes can be grooved or chamfered. 
Also the whole tube can be colour-coated both for aesthetic and corrosive purposes. 
The company is commercializing its products all around Europe taking advantage of the wide footprint of 
the Division all around the continent. 
AM Iasi is immersed in a set of actions with the goal of modernizing the plant, gaining productivity, and 
increasing the quality of their products as well as improving their environmental impact. 
Furthermore, a Product Development Team has been recently constituted in the plant in order to boost 
Product and Process Development projects in a coordinated manner within the AMTP division. 
Role in the project 
AMTP will collaborate in the general coordination in WP1. AMTP will collaborate in the heat plant needs 
definition at WP2. AMPT will help with the tests definition to be carried out during WP7. AMTP will also 
provide data for the sustainability assessment of the project as end -user in WP8. Finally, AMTP will 
collaborate in general activities of communication, dissemination and exploitation activities in WP9.  
Key personnel 
• Romel Nedelcu (M) is Maintenance Manager in AM Iasi. He is Graduate Engineer. Over 29 of working

● One of the most valuable products for AM Iasi are the colour-coated pipes where a tubular pipe (for 
the conveyance of a fluid) is coated externally by a coloured layer that normally adds both an aesthetic 
appearance (making it easily identifiable in a piping system) and an anti-corrosion resistance. Very recently 
a new colour-coating station has been acquired increasing not only the plant’s capacity, but also the variety 
of product finishing as it constitutes a new technology for the company. 
Previous projects / activities related to the subject of this proposal 
Even though this project would be the first EU funding project of AM Iasi, the whole division as well as 
Gorka Iglesias have previous experience in European projects/proposals management: 
● FRISCC – Fire Re sistance of Innovative and Slender Concrete Filled tubular Composite 
Columns (RFCS 2012). Project where the behaviour of tubular columns was deeply analysed in fire 
situations in order to define a new set design method to be included in Eurocode 4. Part 1-2, the referenced 
Code in Europe for the design of composite structural elements. From 01/07/2012 to 30/06/2015 
● HOLLOSSTAB - Overall-Slenderness Based Direct Design for Strength and Stability of 
Innovative Hollow Sections (RFCS 2015). Analysis of slender columns (mainly of high strength steel) 
behaviour under compression or compression + bending loading in order to define a new design method for 
such structural elements, avoiding the current cross -section classification and optimizing the structural 
capacity of tubular columns. From 01/07/2016 to 30/06/2019 
● INNO3DJOINTS - INNOvative 3D JOINTS for robust and economic  hybrid tubular 
construction (RFCS 2016). Development of innovative plug -and-play joints for hybrid tubular 
construction, whereby tubular columns are combined with cold-formed lightweight steel profiles to provide 
a highly efficient structural system. From 01/07/2017 to 30/06/2020 
Significant infrastructure and major items of equipment, relevant to the project 
As already mentioned, one of the key finishing for the AM Iasi’s products is the so -called colour coating, 
consisting on a thin layer of (epoxy, water -based, thermoplastic, etc.) coloured protective/decorative 
material covering the whole tube external surface. For the proper application and fixation of the coating the 
tubes need to be pre-heated at different temperatures depending on the kind of coating to be applied. 
In particular, for the purpose of this project, the newly acquired powder colour coating equipment is 
considered. Here, the tubes need to be pre-heated to a temperature of 200oC. 
The equipment is able to produce CCT using powder technology for epoxy powder coating - min 80 microns/ 
layer and also thermoplastic powder coating - 120 microns/layer.
